Some say the rebels are no longer capable of attacking Bangkok, as many of their leaders have already been captured.

Citizens who had sought refuge within the city from the outskirts have largely returned to their homes, and shops have resumed normal operations. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Bangkok: This afternoon at 5:00 PM, the Siamese government announced that the rebellion has been quelled. The rebel forces have scattered northward in disarray, and the whereabouts of their leaders are largely unknown. Government officials are currently working to restore normalcy, with particular emphasis on repairing the damaged state-owned railways. (19th National Telegram)

(New York) Rumors circulated in the exchange market today that France would abandon the gold standard, causing European currencies to weaken considerably. The franc opened at 5.80 and closed at 5.52. The pound also fell from 4.6116 to 4.5025. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Japanese Complete Survey of Manchuria and Mongolia 40

Rich Resources of Jehol No Longer Ours 41

(Dalian) The Manchurian-Mongolian Academic Survey Team, led by Dr. Tetsu Chen and consisting of eight members, departed from Tokyo and spent ninety days conducting chemical surveys in Mongolia and Jehol. They returned east on the Baikal Maru on the 18th. According to Dr. Nagai's statement to reporters, the actual survey lasted seventy days, during which they faced numerous dangers. The results of the survey exceeded expectations, which is a point of pride for the team. He stated that Jehol is extremely rich in mineral resources such as petroleum, iron, gold, and copper. However, due to orders from the authorities, he cannot disclose specific details. The areas visited by the team had never been surveyed by anyone before, and the resulting findings are sure to impress the world. This type of comprehensive exploration is unprecedented and will continue annually in the future. In addition to the mineral resources, all other findings will be published. (18th Dentsu Telegram)

Page 7

US to Control Capital: New Monetary Policy Delayed - Roosevelt Raises Farm Produce Prices 42

(Washington) Based on various indications, the authorities seem to have a more urgent approach to the recovery movement than before. It is likely that in addition to wages, prices, and production, capital will also be subject to government control. People in business circles believe this is uncertain, and the authorities have new restrictions on issuing new bonds, making it difficult to use capital. The authorities have responded to this criticism by issuing a statement saying that they will no longer allow the free use of money. As a result, it is believed that banks, securities, and commodity exchanges will all be subject to strict control. At the same time, according to figures obtained at the statisticians' conference, the increase in distribution of manufactured goods in September was less than the total amount of seasonal sales, about 11% less than in 1932. The authorities are now actively pursuing a campaign to buy promptly, in order to expand sales. The Edison Company in New Jersey is giving each employee an additional five dollars on top of their weekly wages, urging them to spend it immediately to stimulate trade. It is generally believed that the recent slowdown in business is a reaction to the artificial boom of early summer. However, the number of unemployed has indeed decreased. Labor Secretary Frances Perkins stated that 620,000 people regained employment in September. Since March of this year, the number of unemployed has decreased by 2.7 million, and weekly wages have increased by $64 million. President Roosevelt is now refusing to allow the import of medicinal alcohol, and has rejected proposals to allow it to be imported and stored for release around December 21st, when Prohibition is lifted. Merchants have recently requested temporary permission to import three million gallons of medicinal alcohol for Christmas sales. (19th Reuters Telegram)

(Washington) Monetary expert Griswold wrote an article for the Associated Press stating that the President's advisors have studied more than fifty monetary plans submitted by various parties, and have now narrowed them down to three or four, all based on sound money principles. They do not want to use greenbacks or treasury bills to raise prices. These plans are being studied in detail so that they can be presented to the President. According to official sources, the government originally intended to announce its monetary policy this week, but this has been delayed due to the sudden drop in farm product prices. It is now expected that no announcement will be made until the prices recover to a level deemed satisfactory by the government. However, there is currently no danger of currency inflation. Steps to stabilize the gold dollar and gold pound have already begun, but are not being rushed. Some advisors admit that a return to a revised gold standard may not be possible before next spring, and the timing of its return will depend on the overall state of industry and commerce. (18th National Telegram)

(Washington) It has been learned that the US President will soon provide a new stimulus to increase farm product prices, so that they can match the rise in manufactured goods prices. The President

considers the 1921-1926 prices as the standard. The average price in September of this year was only 70.8% of that standard, and the average price in August was 69.5%, but it has risen by an average of 18% compared to February. (18th National Press Telegram)

Simla Conference: India Makes Demands - Japan Deems Them Unacceptable 43

(Tokyo) Official telegrams regarding the negotiations at the Simla Conference on the 17th arrived at the Foreign Ministry yesterday. The Indian representatives made the following proposals to Japan: (1) The allocated quantity of Japanese cotton cloth imports should be 320 million square yards. (2) Japan's purchase quantity of Indian cotton should be 130,000 bales. (3) India will reduce the cotton cloth tariff to 52.5%. (4) The increase or decrease in the quantity of Japanese cotton cloth imports and the quantity of Indian cotton purchased should be linked to each other, adopting the so-called Sliding Scale system. (5) Reduce tariffs based on the above quantities. (6) Aside from preferential treatment for the British Empire, no discriminatory treatment should be applied to other foreign countries. Japan should be granted most-favored-nation status. Representative Sawada refuted these proposals, saying that India's proposals were far removed from Japan's proposals, especially the linking of Japanese cotton cloth import quantities and Indian cotton purchase quantities, which Japan absolutely opposed. He requested that Japan's proposals be used as the basis for a compromise proposal. Governor Bowyer also rose to refute this. The meeting ended at this point. (19th Dentsu Telegram)

Simla: As a result of the Japanese-Indian government meeting on the 17th, there was still a considerable gap between the proposals of the two sides. It was expected that the meeting between Representative Sawada and Governor Bowyer would find a solution. Yesterday morning, Representative Sawada, accompanied by Officer Matsushima, visited Governor Bowyer at his private residence and held the first private meeting, lasting for one hour. He left at noon. From this meeting, it can be seen that India is still taking a considerably tough stance. The atmosphere of considering the future relations between Japan and India and seeking a political solution suddenly became strong. In addition, the Japanese side, through this meeting, has learned of India's attitude and is coordinating countermeasures and telegraphing the home ministry for instructions. Therefore, the government representatives' meeting scheduled for the 19th has been temporarily suspended. (19th Dentsu Telegram)

Shidehara Compiling History of Japanese Diplomacy 44

▲As a Lifelong Undertaking

(Tokyo) Japan has never had the compilation of an authoritative diplomatic history. Diplomatic records since the opening of the country are secretly stored in the Foreign Ministry archives and are not allowed to be made public. Former Foreign Minister Kijūrō Shidehara recently decided to gather various materials and complete a major diplomatic history as a lifelong undertaking, with a budget of 150,000 yen and a five-year plan. (19th Japan United Press Telegram)

Overview of the Bandit Areas in Jiangxi and Fujian 61

(Nanchang) The so-called "Chinese Soviet Republic" composed of southern Jiangxi and northern Fujian used to export tobacco, sugarcane, and indigo before the government forces implemented a blockade. The inland areas were mostly self-sufficient in grain, but did not produce salt. Its capital is Ruijin, where the Central Committee appointed by the "Executive Committee of the Chinese Communist Party" is stationed. Mao Zedong is also in Ruijin. The National Government has now offered a reward of 100,000 yuan for his head. Mao is a young man of 32, suffering from lung disease, and it is feared that he will not live long. Mao has established a Workers' and Peasants' Bank in Ruijin and issued 20 million yuan in paper money. Its branches are located in Zhu De's headquarters to facilitate the army's exchange for daily necessities. The mint issues new 20-cent silver coins every year.

The silver coins are minted with an image of Marx on one side and a Communist Party symbol of a sickle and axe on the other. Ruijin now has a Lenin Normal School and a People's School, as well as a political and military school. Its organization is similar to that established by Borodin in Guangzhou. There is now a hospital and two treatment centers. It was originally planned to build a number of public hospitals, but this could not be realized due to the lack of medicine and other supplies after the National Army implemented a blockade. The bandits now organize their own post offices and issue five-cent stamps, which are engraved with the Communist sickle symbol. They also publish a newspaper called "Central Red Light News." The old county boundaries are still retained, but each village and county has an organization of the Soviet and Executive Committee, exercising powers under the supervision of the Communist Party representatives. The registration of the people is divided into several age groups: 10 to 15, 15 to 20, 20 to 40, and 40 to 60. The people must obey the orders of the Party, and everyone is forced to undertake some kind of work. All land deeds of the people have been destroyed, and the land has been re-allocated. The method is that 30% belongs to the Farmers' Association, 30% to the state, and 40% to the landlords. Each household is limited to 20 mu of land. However, the Farmers' Association has already failed, because most of the land of the association has been leased to individuals for cultivation. As for the land belonging to the government, it is all wasteland and mountain areas. The products obtained by the farmers can only be sold by cooperative shops on behalf of the farmers at extremely low prices. They can only retain the rice and grain to supply themselves, so the farmers mostly feel the inequality of this treatment, but under the red terror, there is nothing they can do. The property in the cities has also been treated in the same way, divided into various areas and evenly distributed to each household for living. The operation of various shops is based on the Soviet cooperative theory, with no distinction between shop owners and shop assistants. Shop owners also only serve in the shop as employees, because all the shops have also been confiscated by the state, and the prices of various items are also managed by the state, so there is no profit to be made. Each person is only allowed to deposit 50 yuan in cash. The practice of the eldest son inheriting property, which has been practiced in China for thousands of years, is absolutely prohibited. There is no talk of filial piety to parents. All children over the age of ten are forced to enter the "Workers' and Peasants' Military School" to receive training, learn to sing the Internationale, and carry out propaganda work. They also form children's corps and often send them to the front line to confront the National Army. These children must leave their hometowns to receive training, and in order to cultivate the cruelty of young children, those who violate party rules in the Red Army are ordered to be executed by these children. Those aged 15 to 20 are incorporated into the "Red Guards," and then incorporated into the regular army. These troops are guided by youths from Moscow or the Belorussian Lenin University. In 1931, there were about 200 such young military officers who infiltrated Jiangxi Province. There are now no Russian advisors, because the Red Army thinks it is not needed. The finances of the Communist bandits, even if supplied by Moscow, are not enough, so they use the confiscated cash to issue paper money. (17th Reuters Telegram)

Plan for Reorganizing Chinese Seamen 76

(Nanjing) Plan for reorganizing Chinese seamen: (1) Seamen must be qualified personnel; (2) Non-seamen are not allowed to work as seamen on steamships; (3) When seamen obtain certificates, local seamen's branches must hire experts with seaman skills to conduct face-to-face assessments of their qualifications, and submit qualified applicants to the headquarters for review and issuance; (4) The assessment of seamen includes oral tests and practical operations; (5) When companies and shipping bureaus hire seamen, they must consult with the seamen's union. The union will be responsible to the employers. If dismissals or replacements are necessary, they must also consult with the union. If there are disputes between employers and the union, they can be resolved through joint consultation with party and government agencies. (19th Central News Agency)

No Need to Issue Separate Regulations for Land Tax 78

Inner Mongolian Princes and Nobles Hold Meeting at Bailing Temple; Prince De Exploited and Inciting Autonomy; Princes and Nobles Extremely Dissatisfied with Prince De; Songshishi Takayoshi Incites Riots in Duolun 93

Beiping Correspondence: Inner Mongolia is divided into three parts: Eastern Mongolia, Central Mongolia, and Western Mongolia. Zhaowuda League within Rehe Province is Eastern Mongolia. Five Banners and ten Flags of Xilingol League within Chahar Province, and four Left Wing Banners of Chahar are Central Mongolia. Four Banners and six Flags of Ulanqab League in Suiyuan, seven Flags of Yikezhao League, two Left and Right Wing Flags of Shumeite Tribe, and four Right Wing Flags of Chahar Tribe are Western Mongolia. Since the loss of Rehe, Eastern Mongolia's connection has already been severed. Central and Western Mongolia still maintain their original relations. Recently, Prince De, the Deputy Leader of Xilingol League in Central Mongolia, has been exploited and is advocating autonomy, which has become a problem and is attracting attention from all sides.

The knowledge of the Mongolian people is unsophisticated. During the feudal era, the income from herding livestock throughout the year was entirely used to support the princes and nobles. In recent years, more and more young Mongolians have resided in the interior, and those with higher levels of knowledge have felt the desire to break away from the shackles of the prince system and obtain true freedom. The autonomy movement is gradually emerging. Prince De, although having less seniority among the general princes, is relatively cunning. Recently, he has been exploited by a certain party, thinking of seizing power. On one hand, he is trying to win over the Panchen Lama to use as a means of rallying support. On the other hand, he is chanting loudly for autonomy to win over the public's favor. However, most princes and nobles are fully aware of the situation and are not fooled. And the more knowledgeable Mongolian people also believe that the proposed autonomy regulations are contrary to what the Mongolian people hope for, adding another layer of shackles to the Mongolian people. They are cursing and reviling each other. Therefore, Prince De convened a meeting for the first time at Bailing Temple to discuss the topic of autonomy, but very few people attended, and there were no results. He then changed the date to convene another meeting on the 28th of last month. When the time came, the meeting could not be held again due to too few people. It was not until the 9th of this month that the assembly was held, but there were still no results. On the 13th, another meeting was held, attended by six princes and more than fifty Beizi and Beile. Most of the princes, Beizi and Beile attended the meeting to pay homage to the Panchen Lama, and very few were truly called by Prince De. Before the meeting, Prince De drafted autonomy regulations and proposed organizing an autonomous organization at an appropriate location. Prince Zhuo, Prince Suo, Prince Yang, and others opposed Prince De's actions, which had a strong background. The other princes and Beile remained silent. Seeing that the atmosphere at the meeting was not good, Prince De said that anyone who did not speak would be considered to have tacitly agreed. However, no one spoke. The meeting lasted for several hours and again produced no results. However, after the meeting, Prince De even issued a declaration in the name of the leader, stating that the leagues and banners of Inner Mongolia would organize an autonomous government and implement a high degree of autonomy. His ambitions have not ended, and he is thinking of actively proceeding. According to observations from all sides, most Inner Mongolian princes and the general public, except for Prince De, strongly support the central government and are quite dissatisfied with Prince De being instigated. However, under the current complex situation, if the central government cannot take appropriate measures, the temptation of external forces and the incitement from within can also be sufficient to initiate changes. Songshishi Takayoshi, the director of the Kwantung Army's special mission in Rehe, went to Duolun before Prince De convened the meeting and invited the Inner Mongolian princes to talk, with sinister incitement. He has not yet left Duolun, and his intentions are frightening. (October 17)

Panchen Lama Discusses Reasons for Inner Mongolian Autonomy; Yan Xishan Sends Shi Huayan to Meet with the Panchen Lama; Panchen Lama Hopes Central Government Officials Will Go to Mongolia Soon 94

Suiyuan Correspondence: Shi Huayan, the Director of Suiyuan Reclamation, was dispatched by telegram by Yan Xishan and accompanied by Ding Wangduoji, the Director of the Panchen Lama's Office in Suiyuan, to pay homage to the Panchen Lama at Siziwang Banner by car. Shi and others have now returned to Suiyuan yesterday (the 13th). According to their account, the details of the trip and the situation of Inner Mongolian autonomy are roughly as follows: Shi said that Yan Director (Xishan) and Fu Chairman (Zuoyi) sent him (Shi's self-reference) to inquire about the Panchen Lama's well-being because the Panchen Lama had been proclaiming in the western frontier for many years without resting. They recently heard that the master had returned to Siziwang Mansion from Xilin Gol League. On the morning of the 9th of this month, he set off from Suiyuan by car with Ding Wangduoji, the Director of the Panchen Lama's Office in Suiyuan, passing through Wuchuan County and Niaolanhua, and arriving at Siziwang Mansion at 5 PM. Unexpectedly, the Panchen Lama had already moved to Xialamuoluo Temple to chant scriptures at 11 AM that morning. The temple was more than ninety miles northwest of the Mansion. He and others continued to travel there, but it was already late when they arrived at Gegen Temple, so they stayed there. The temple was more than twenty miles away from Xialamuoluo Temple. They were warmly received by the temple's managing lama, Nierba. The next morning, they set off again at 7 AM and arrived at Xialamuoluo Temple at 10 AM. At 2 PM, they paid homage to the Panchen Lama. They noted that the hairs on the Panchen Lama's face were more gray than the last time they saw him in Suiyuan. They asked the Panchen Lama about his experiences in proclaiming the Dharma in Xilin Gol League and the current situation of Inner Mongolian

Autonomy. The Panchen Lama replied that he had been to Xilin Gol League four times in total. The first time was when the banners of Xilin Gol League invited him to preach the Dharma. The second time was when the banners of Xilin Gol League invited him to recite the Kalachakra Tantra. He originally planned to spend the winter at Beizi Temple at the request of the League Banners, but before winter came, the Hailar Incident occurred, and Deputy Commander Zhang Hanqing sent someone to invite him to Shenyang for seventeen days to help resolve the Hailar issue. After the issue was resolved, he was invited to recite scriptures by Guitutong and Solun Banner. Then the September 18th Incident occurred, and he had no choice but to return from Liaoyang, passing through the border of Outer Mongolia and passing through Xilin Gol League once. This was the fourth time he had been to Xilin Gol League. He was originally invited by Su Wang (i.e., the Head of Xilin Gol League) to recite scriptures. He sent someone to invite him in January, but he did not go until May because he had not finished reciting scriptures in the western banners. Just then, the autonomy issue arose. He observed that the reasons were (1) There were many gaps in affection between that place and the interior; (2) They were influenced by Outer Mongolia and Eastern Mongolia; (3) It was due to the Chahar Incident. The Mongolian princes had said to him that doing so could increase self-defense strength and consolidate border defense. He had been stationed there for a long time and observed that most princes and people were still inclined towards the central government and hoped that Minister Huang and Vice Chairman Zhao would come soon to discuss and formulate sound and concrete measures. The next day, they rested at the temple and saw the Panchen Lama's Great Khenpos and the temple's Living Buddha, Bolerdengdan Cijiasheng. At the same time, they also saw Siziwang and chatted very happily. On the third day (the 12th) morning, they bid farewell to the Panchen Lama. They set off at 3 PM and returned to Suiyuan yesterday (the 13th) at 4 PM. (14th)

Situation of Bloody Battles Between Soldiers and Bandits on the Border of Jiangxi and Fujian; Battles in Lichuan, Nancheng, and Yihuang; Bandits Collapse on All Fronts and Retreat Eastward 95

Nanchang Correspondence: Xiao Jingxian, the commander-in-chief of the bogus Jiangxi-Fujian army, withdrew from Lichuan on the 28th of last month with the remnants of Fang Shao's bandits. At the same time, Peng Dehuai of the 3rd Army Corps, Lin Biao of the bogus 1st Army Corps, and Luo Binghui of the bogus 12th Army Corps suffered disastrous defeats in their attacks on Shaowu and Yanping. Zhu and Mao then ordered the bandits to concentrate in Guangze and advance on Lichuan through Shanguan and Xieshi, attempting a desperate gamble to break through eastern Jiangxi and spy on Fuzhou. However, the anti-bandit army's 囗 column of the northern route, Zhou Hunyuan's 囗 division and the 囗囗 division, had already captured Lichuan and seized Peng Dehuai's letter to Xiao Jingxian, learning of the bandits' conspiracy. They immediately deployed heavy troops to defend. By the beginning of this month, Zhu and Mao secretly concentrated the main forces from northern Fujian and advanced from the Shanguan and Xieshi areas, still using the strategy of concentrating their main forces on one point to attack part of the national army. They advanced towards Xunqiao in Lichuan, Xiaoshi in Nancheng, and Xinfeng Street, a transportation hub between Nancheng and Nanfeng. Yao Chun, Zhou Hunyuan, Wu Qiwu, Zhou Yan, and other units of the national army engaged in battle separately, bravely fighting back. Battles occurred in Lichuan, Nancheng, Nanfeng, and Zixi and the eastern regions. From the 10th to the 13th, blood battles lasted for four days and nights, and many bandits were killed. Yesterday, military sources said that the battle in Lichuan was over and the bandits had retreated eastward. The battles in Nancheng and Nanfeng are still raging. At the same time, there was also contact in Yihuang. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has sent a telegram to commend the armies participating in this battle, which shows the urgency of the situation at that time. The following is a record of the telegram: "According to Chief Commander Chen's repeated telegrams from Army Commander Zhou Yuxu, Qi Jiaheng, and others, our division's Ge Zhongshan brigade made a surprise attack from Lichuan, penetrated Feiyuan, and defeated the bandit army. On the way back to Xunqiao, it was ambushed by the main forces of the bogus 3rd Army Corps and the bogus 7th Army Corps. After fierce fighting for one day and night, it was rescued by friendly forces and the 31st Regiment was brought back to Lichuan. The 34th Regiment was isolated in Xunqiao and fought independently for five days and nights. With food and ammunition exhausted, they fought in hand-to-hand combat, relying on villages to defend and wait for rescue. At this time, our 囗囗 and 囗囗 divisions learned of the regiment's isolation and organized a commando to rush to the rescue, which was able to thwart the enemy's offensive and allow the entire regiment to withdraw. After investigation, it was found that Regiment Commander Weng was able to resist tens of thousands of bandits with the strength of one regiment for four or five days, and the officers and soldiers of the two divisions of 囗囗 and 囗囗 were able to rescue them despite the great risks and without missing the opportunity. This could not have been achieved without daily training and inherent loyalty and bravery. Upon hearing the report, I am deeply gratified and will give generous rewards and condolences separately to encourage them. (1) In this battle of Xunqiao, the 34th Regiment of the Ge Brigade is requested by the Central Party Department to be specially awarded the most glorious flag of bandit suppression to show their special merits. (2) The officers of the commando and Regiment Commander Weng of the two divisions of 囗囗 will be promoted one rank each, and each soldier will receive one month's extra pay. (3) The casualties of the commando and Regiment Commander Weng's officers and soldiers will be investigated and reported to be given double injury bonuses and condolence money, and honorable titles will be posthumously awarded. A telegram will also be sent to the anti-bandit forces, and in future anti-bandit operations, they should all have the spirit of adventure and hardship of our army's Weng Regiment and the commando, so that the team will not be the only ones with merit, and there are high hopes." (18th)

[P Hua County Still Urgently Awaits Rescue; Yellow River Water Still Rises Occasionally; Number of Refugees Increases Daily

Kaifeng Correspondence: The disaster situation in Hua County is extremely dire. Appeals have been made to all parties for relief, but the Yellow River water has risen again, and rescue is still urgently needed. Therefore, the Hua County Flood Relief Association recently sent another telegram to various parties appealing for relief, with extremely sincere words. The original text is as follows: "Since the Yellow River flooded Hua County, half of the county has been destroyed, and people have been drifting and displaced for more than two months. The tragic situation has been reported by telegram, and we have been grateful that the various Xian and good groups have sent personnel to investigate and provide relief. However, the River God is merciless, and the water volume rises occasionally. The great flood directly penetrates Hua County. Six hundred villages that could be crossed on foot have become a lake. Three hundred thousand people are still living in treetops. Silt blocks the roads, and there is no way to escape. They eat in the wind and sleep in the open, waiting to die. Fires have been extinguished, and cries are heard from time to time. News of deaths is frequent, and it is heartbreaking to speak of. Since the fish have risen in the past two days, the remaining survivors have fled one after another, supporting the old and carrying the young, coming one after another. Families that were once wealthy are now destitute. They are emaciated and unrecognizable to relatives and friends. Cries of hunger and cold are unbearable to hear. The number of people in the various shelters is increasing daily. The 3,000 stone of grain from the local donations has already been eaten more than half. It is estimated that it will be used up in ten days. Resources have been exhausted and there are no ways to remedy the situation. If we allow them to disperse, starvation is inevitable, and security is worrisome. We beg you to quickly provide urgent relief and release one yuan to save one life. No matter how much or how little, it is all a saving grace. If the disaster victims do not die, they will all praise the living Buddha. With tears in our eyes, we present our words and await orders in extreme sorrow. The Hua County Flood Relief Association bows in respect," (13th)

Meng Gu, a resident of the Mengjiazhai in the southeast of Nanxiang, was over sixty years old and owned more than ten mu of good farmland. Her sons and daughters-in-law had died early, and she lived alone. On the 13th night, thieves went to rob her, stabbing her to death and abandoning her body in a cotton field. The next morning, neighbors, not seeing Gu, went to her house to check and found the door open and the boxes overturned, and realized that something had happened. Suzhou: Police and Bandits Exchange Fire at Shiliting 97

Bao Sheng, from Baoying, and his nephew Gu Ruyi, sailed from their hometown to Suzhou to purchase cowhide for making wooden clogs. Eight fellow villagers, men and women, including Gu Yongtai, Luo Zhu, and Wang Wu, also came to Suzhou to work as hired laborers, so they came on the same boat. Unexpectedly, the boat was already near the suburbs of Suzhou, in the Baiyang Bay area of ​​Shiliting, when a bandit boat suddenly came from a branch harbor, fired a gun, and ordered them to stop. As a result, the ten people on board were searched, and then driven ashore. The bandits shook the boat and stolen goods away. Gu and others reported to the Third Public Security Sub-office. Inspector Zhang Lesan led the police to advance by land and water, and surrounded them from left and right. The two sides exchanged fire. After half an hour, the bandits could not hold on, abandoned the boat and fled ashore without being captured. Only the original boat and a bandit boat were shaken back to the office. Upon checking the lost items, only dozens of dollars in cash and more than a dozen pieces of clothing were found. The office then escorted the ten people from the entire case to the Third Bureau for questioning. After interrogation, they were all released on bail to retrieve their belongings.

Impersonating a Corpse's Family, Opening the Coffin for Examination

A bather wearing a Zhongshan suit with a Hubei accent came to the Tianyi Pool Bathhouse outside Changmen the day before yesterday (the 14th). After entering the pool, he suddenly fainted in the pool. The hall manager, Hang Zilong, hired a car to send him to the hospital, but he died on the way. The body was dragged back to Tianyi Pool. Afterwards, Zhang Xiaosan, a boatman who lived near the Hubei Guild Hall, said that the deceased's name was Zhang Minggan, and he was his cousin. He had been suffering from asthma, which caused his tragic death this time. He then filed a petition with the court to waive the examination. Zhang then took the corpse and had it coffined and buried. On the 18th, the 32nd Branch of the Public Security Bureau in charge of the area suspected that the case was highly suspicious. When Zhang Xiaosan was summoned for questioning, he stammered. Later, he confessed that his surname was actually Zhang. Because the deceased was a fellow villager, he had impersonated a relative to avoid the tragedy of being examined. The land guard, Xu Yong'an, and the car driver, Jiang Mingfu, who dragged the dead man, were also escorted to the court to await interrogation. Yesterday (the 19th), the court sent a prosecutor to open the coffin for examination. Although the examination proved that the deceased did die from suffocation and there was no other cause, the bizarre news of impersonating the dead man's family has spread throughout society.

Changshu: Store Clerk Castrates Himself in Suicide 99

Gu Suizhi, residing in the Lao Wu Shi town of this county, is

currently 46 years old. He married Chen, and they had two children. After Chen's death, Gu remarried Zhao. Nine years ago, Gu came to Changshu and worked as a clerk in the Yi Ji foreign goods company. His family resided at number 29 Yin Xian Street. Gu had been diligent and resourceful for seven years and four months and maintained his position. However, the store underwent reorganization last winter, leading to his unemployment. Gu's family was already poor, and he was subjected to ridicule, causing him great resentment. Recently, he contracted malaria and lacked the funds for treatment, leading him to contemplate suicide. On the 16th night, he suddenly bought several catties of yellow wine and drank alone, forcing his wife to sleep first. He then used scissors to cut off his testicles in an attempt to kill himself. However, due to his strong constitution, he failed. He then used the scissors to cut his throat and stabbed himself several times in the abdomen. His wife heard the noise and quickly lit a lamp to find her husband lying in a pool of blood. She cried loudly, waking the neighbors, who rushed him to the Yu He Hospital. Doctors at the hospital bandaged his wounds. He began to regain consciousness around 9 o'clock, and his mind was clear. However, it is said that his life remains in danger.

Failure to Conjure Silver from Tin Leads to Imprisonment

Shen Tianfu, the young master of Shen Changyuan rice store in Qingyang Town, Jiangyin, met Liu Zishan, a rice broker from Shanghai, (also known as Li Zishan, also named Cheng Fushou, a native of Xue Si Niang Bridge in Dang Kou) and Wang Fuxing on a train in August of the 20th year. Wang took out many mineral-like objects and told Shen that these minerals could be alchemized into silver using a medicinal liquid, yielding substantial profits. However, the medicinal liquid was in short supply, and the place of sale was very secretive, and the price was also expensive, and it must be purchased in person to be obtained. Shen was secretly pleased upon hearing this and invited Liu and others to his home to experiment. After Liu used the medicinal liquid to conjure, it did turn into silver. In fact, the test item was indeed real silver, and the rest were all tin and copper. Shen did not realize the fraud and was overjoyed. He immediately paid Liu and others 1,150 silver dollars, instructing them to go to Shanghai to purchase the medicinal liquid and return to Wuxi to conjure more. However, Liu and others never returned. Shen then realized he had been deceived. Until the other day, Shen encountered Liu Zishan in Sheng Alley in this county and

dragged him to the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau, who transferred him to the county court. After Chief Zhou held a trial, Shen Tianfu was ordered to return home, and Liu Zishan was detained to await further investigation.

Changzhou: Malignant Malaria Spreads in the North of the City 101

Recently, malignant malaria has been discovered in Wu County. The symptoms include persistent high fever, which does not subside with sweating. The symptoms are very similar to typhoid fever and cannot be confirmed without a blood test. Traditional Chinese medicine practitioners often mistake this disease for typhoid fever or damp-heat. This disease is very dangerous. The bacteria invade the brain, causing madness, similar to meningitis, eventually leading to coma and death. The origin of this disease is likely due to transmission by venomous mosquitoes. If treated properly in the early stages, there is no danger to life. However, in recent days, there have been many patients in the north of the city and elsewhere, and the disease is spreading. Countless people have died in vain.

Yangzhou: Water Police Brigade Embezzles a Large Amount of Opium 103

Regarding the case of the 23rd Brigade of the 6th District of the Water Police stationed in Xiannv Temple seizing a large quantity of opium, it is now known that this opium consists of 334 packages, each weighing 50 taels, with a total value of over 30,000 gold pieces. The brigade only delivered 160 packages to the Guazhou district headquarters. At that time, the district headquarters had already apprehended a certain adjutant of a unit escorting this opium from Hankou. His weapons were immediately confiscated, and a shipping invoice for 334 packages was found on his person. It was then believed that the 23rd Brigade had embezzled too much. Inspector Xing was immediately dispatched with a team on the Huai'an warship to Xiannv to investigate. The brigade's leader, Tuo, then handed over another 111 packages, leaving 60 packages missing. It is claimed that these have been used as rewards for the informant. The disposition of the case is not yet known. However, it is rumored that the opium was transported from Hankou by Jiang Songyan, a major opium dealer from Fanchuan. According to reports, Jiang had previously transported 63 boxes of opium, which were seized and divided up by the Public Security Bureau of the Seventh District of this county. The provincial government issued a circular order for strict arrest, but the case has not yet been closed.

Hangzhou: Completion of the Lingshan River Railway Bridge on the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway 104

The newly built Lingshan River Railway Bridge on the Jinyu section of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway spans the Lingshan River at Jiming Rock, south of Longyou South Gate. It has seven spans, totaling over 660 feet in length. The bridge piers are made of concrete, and the bridge beams and deck are made of steel, with a total weight of approximately 200 tons. The entire bridge pier and deck engineering was contracted by Shanghai Yangzi Construction Company. The steel materials used were specially ordered from famous German factories. The total cost is over 110,000 yuan, and the official opening is scheduled for the 21st of this month.

Fire in Baoji Guan Alley Last Night

Zhang A'yang, a resident of No. 16 Baoji Guan Alley in Hangzhou, operates a foreign textile business. At 7:15 p.m. on the 18th, Zhang was out on business and had not returned. His wife went upstairs to sleep, but the kerosene lamp accidentally overturned, igniting the bed curtains. The fire was fierce. Fortunately, the fire brigade and fire engines rushed to the scene to put out the fire. It took half an hour to extinguish the fire. A total of two houses belonging to the Zhu Wu family at No. 18 were burned down, resulting in a loss of approximately over 1,000 yuan.

Jiashan: Clash of Laborers and Disturbance of Road Workers 105

This county has repeatedly received provincial orders to recruit 100 conscripts to be transferred to the bandit suppression army in Jiangxi. However, due to the difficulty of handling the matter and the inability to recruit, the province was requested to reduce the quota to 50 conscripts, but the handling still felt difficult. The Public Security Bureau, compelled by the provincial order, had no choice but to change the recruitment to a draft. The Second District was required to draft five conscripts, which were forcibly drafted the night before (17th). One of them, Li A'si, was a railroad worker who was already old. Therefore, the railroad workers requested an exemption from conscription. However, the branch bureau did not grant their request. The railroad workers were enraged and forcibly took Li A'si back. A conflict broke out, and all the workshop rooms, sloping glass, tables, chairs, and utensils were destroyed. One of the road workers was injured. The road workers became even more enraged and gathered over 40 followers, tying up all the police officers. The branch bureau chief rushed to the scene upon hearing the news, intending to mediate. However, the road workers were overwhelming and surrounded the branch bureau chief, intending to beat him severely. The station master rushed to persuade them, but to no avail. The railway department's inspector happened to be in Feng, and the county government also received a telegram notifying them that the incident was expanding. The county immediately dispatched Police Brigade Captain Wang Jikang, leading many police officers, to join Public Security Bureau Chief Xu Yanwu. Only then did the Xu branch bureau chief escape danger. The authorities demanded that the station master hand over the troublemaking workers to the county for severe punishment. The road workers reported to the engineering office and the Shanghai-Hangzhou section inspector, demanding a satisfactory resolution, or they would all go on strike as a threat.

We believe that your newspaper's reporting is inaccurate and should be corrected. Sincerely, Central Aviation School, October 17th

Capital Ferry to Open the Day After Tomorrow; Direct Shanghai-Beiping Train to Be Implemented Simultaneously; Train No. 202 to Cross the River on Opening Day; Prices Set, Faster Train Ticket Prices Between Tianjin and Beiping; Joint Freight Train Between Shanghai and Beiping to Run Once a Day 107

The Shanghai-Beiping joint freight service has been implemented on September 1st. The Capital Ferry is scheduled to hold an opening ceremony the day after tomorrow. The Shanghai-Beiping direct train service, after trial runs, is scheduled to be implemented simultaneously the day after tomorrow. According to details obtained by a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency:

Direct Train Service 108

The Railway Department has decided to hold the opening ceremony of the Capital Yangtze River Ferry on the afternoon of the 22nd of this month at 2:00 PM. The Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration has specially dispatched Xie Wenlong, Deputy Director of the Transportation Department, to go to Beiping on the Shanghai-Nanjing overnight express train tomorrow to attend the opening ceremony. The Shanghai-Beiping direct train service will be implemented immediately after the ceremony. Train No. 303, the Shanghai-Beiping through train departing from Beiping at 7:15 AM on the 21st, will arrive at Pukou at 3:05 PM on the 22nd. It will depart from Pukou at 11:00 AM and arrive in Beiping at 8:48 PM on the 24th.

A Total of Seven Trains 109

If it cannot be completed in time, the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway will temporarily borrow a train from the Tianjin-Pukou and Beiping-Liaoning Railways, which is the train that arrived in Shanghai and stopped at Shanghai North Station for a trial run the day before yesterday.

Train Service Prices 110

On the day the direct train service is implemented, the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway will also begin selling second-class sleeper car tickets, and the Beiping-Liaoning Railway will simultaneously increase the special express train fare between Beiping and Tianjin. The train service prices are listed below: Shanghai to Beiping, Beiping to Shanghai, the first-class passenger ticket for both up and down trains is 76.5 yuan, the second-class passenger ticket is 49.5 yuan, the third-class passenger ticket is 24.75 yuan. The upper berth of the first-class sleeper car is 3.5 yuan extra, the lower berth is 4.5 yuan extra. Joint Freight Train 111

All railways have designated joint freight stations for the Shanghai-Beiping joint freight train service. The Railway Department has instructed the Tianjin-Pukou, Beiping-Liaoning, and Shanghai-Nanjing Railways to handle it as appropriate. The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway has designated Trains No. 401 and No. 402 as Shanghai-Beiping joint freight trains, which will be implemented on the day of the Capital Ferry opening ceremony on the 22nd of this month. However, the operation will depend on the amount of freight. It is scheduled to run once a day between Shanghai and Beiping. Train No. 401 departs from Nanjing riverside at 2:45 PM and arrives at Shanghai Meigen Road Station at 6:40 AM the next morning.

Responsible Freight 112

The Railway Department issued an instruction to the various railway bureaus, stating that the purpose of the Ministry's order for all railways to implement responsible freight transportation was originally to facilitate freight merchants and ensure the safety of their goods. If responsible goods are lost or damaged, compensation should be determined and paid quickly in accordance with regulations to show good faith. However, the various railways often use the excuse that the responsibility of the personnel involved has yet to be investigated and processed, which often takes one or two months to decide on compensation. In some cases, even a small portion of the loss involves all the goods, and other parts that have not suffered any loss are also detained. This is clearly contrary to the

original intent of responsible freight and is not the way to protect freight merchants. It should be noted that compensation for losses is the railway's responsibility to the freight merchant, while the responsibility of the personnel involved is an internal matter of the railway and should not be confused. It is now stipulated that compensation must be paid within 20 days from the date the station master receives the "claim for compensation" and must not be delayed. The parts that have not suffered any loss should also be allowed for the freight merchants to pick up first in accordance with regulations. In addition to separate orders, it is hereby urgently ordered that the railway bureau comply with this order.

Ministry of Finance Issues Instruction to Lift Restrictions on Customs, Grain, and Duty-Free Exports to Encourage Trade 113

In recent years, the national agricultural output has been relatively abundant, and grain reserves are plentiful. As a result, the prices of agricultural products have gradually declined, causing great hardship to farmers. In view of this, the government has opened up the rice market and exempted export tariffs. The customs authorities have received instructions from the Ministry of Finance to comply.

Ministry of Finance Instruction 114

Since China opened up to trade with various countries, rice, wheat, and miscellaneous grains have been designated as prohibited items for export. Rice and wheat that have already been imported from overseas are also treated as domestic products and cannot be re-exported. This was originally intended to maintain the people's food supply. However, the situation has changed, and the import of foreign rice and wheat is increasing daily, causing domestic grain prices to fall, even below the cost of production. If the ban on exports continues, it will only make it more difficult for food to circulate and will be detrimental to the rural economy, which will have a significant impact. This is not a suitable approach for the current situation. The Ministry has specially informed the Executive Yuan that the original ban on exporting rice, wheat, and other grains should be lifted and that they should be allowed to be sold and transported freely.

The export taxes, both domestic and foreign, will be exempted to facilitate circulation and benefit agriculture. If it becomes necessary to limit exports in the future, a ban will be re-imposed. This was approved by the 128th meeting of the Executive Yuan, which ordered the Ministry to instruct the customs authorities to comply. In addition to instructing the General Affairs Department to issue an order to the customs commissioners to stop the ban on exporting rice, wheat, sorghum, millet, buckwheat, corn, and other miscellaneous grains that were originally prohibited, and to exempt them from export taxes, this order is hereby issued to the supervisor for compliance.

Flour Industry Conference 115

Flour industry representatives gathered yesterday at the Bank Club on Hong Kong Road to discuss whether the Ministry of Finance's exemption of export taxes on rice and wheat included flour. Furthermore, they noted that the flour market is deteriorating daily, and all factories are on the verge of collapse. They proposed that the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry be requested to grant exemptions from all taxes and levies on flour, in accordance with the grain tax exemption instruction, in order to maintain the industry. The flour industry representatives have submitted the above points to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry for approval.

Japanese Aged Rice Dumped in Shanghai; First Batch of 25,000 Bags Stockpiled at Yongxing Warehouse in Pudong; Shenfeng and Other Eight Rice Merchants Underwrite Second Batch, Loading Already Stopped 116

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that Japan is dumping warehouse-aged rice in China. The Chamber of Commerce has sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry requesting the imposition of rice taxes. The first batch of Japanese rice, totaling 25,000 bags, has arrived in Shanghai and is being stockpiled at Yongxing Warehouse in Pudong. Shenfeng and other eight rice merchants are underwriting the second batch, but loading has already been stopped. Details are as follows:

Dumping of Japanese Rice 117

Japan, facing a backlog of warehouse-aged rice and a bumper harvest of new grains, has decided to sell a total of 50,000 bags of warehouse-aged rice and store new rice instead. However, the sale of aged rice would inevitably lead to a fall in rice prices. To avoid the decline and affect the livelihood of farmers, the aged rice is being dumped in China, entrusted to the Shanghai American company Hanlai Road Foreign Company for sale in Shanghai. After the Ningbo Association received a telegram, it immediately sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to report. The Chamber of Commerce believed that this year's new grains from various provinces would soon be on the market, and if Japanese rice arrived in Shanghai, it would inevitably affect the prices of new rice. Therefore, it sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, urging them to quickly impose taxes on foreign rice.

First Batch Arrives in Shanghai 118

A total of 50,000 bags of Japanese rice,

aged rice from Yangon stockpiled 20

years ago, are being managed by the American company Hanlai Road Foreign Company and sold to eight rice merchants in Shanghai's South City, including Shenfeng, who are distributing and underwriting the rice. Each bag weighs 200 bags, or 150 catties, and is priced at 6.3 yuan per bag in Chinese currency. The rice is being shipped to Shanghai in two batches, with delivery at Shanghai warehouses. The first batch of 25,000 bags has already arrived in Shanghai by Japanese ship and unloaded at Yongxing Warehouse in Lujiazui, Pudong. However, the warehouse is operated by a foreign company, and the warehouse manager is Chinese.

Purchasing Process 119

A Xin Sheng News Agency reporter interviewed Mr. Gu Xinyi of the Bean and Rice Industry Association yesterday. According to him, the Japanese warehouse-aged rice being shipped to Shanghai was purchased by eight rice merchants in Shanghai, totaling 50,000 bags. The reason for the purchase is that the above-mentioned eight rice merchants already had stocks of foreign rice, and they were afraid that the price of foreign rice would fall after the Hanlai Road Foreign Company sold Yangon foreign rice. Moreover, the principle of levying import taxes on foreign rice has been passed and is likely to be implemented. Therefore, they jointly purchased the rice for delivery at Shanghai warehouses.

Negotiations to Stop Loading 120

As for the first batch of Japanese warehouse rice that has already arrived in Shanghai

and been unloaded in Pudong, totaling 25,000

bags, the association has informed the eight merchants that the Yangon rice purchased from the Hanlai Road Foreign Company is actually Japanese warehouse-aged rice. The rice merchants did not know this when they placed the order. After being notified, they immediately negotiated with the Hanlai Road Foreign Company, urging them to quickly send a telegram to Japan to stop loading the second batch of Japanese warehouse rice. It is said that the foreign company has agreed to send a telegram to Japan to stop loading.

Telephone Company's Request for Price Increase; Shanghai Municipal Council Decides to Consider it Slowly; Information Office Releases Original Letter from the Company 121

The Public Utilities Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council discussed the telephone company's request for a price increase on the 13th of this month. After careful consideration, the committee members believed that the telephone company's proposal, in its current form, was not appropriate for approval. However, the financial issues involved in this case are also related to the French Concession Municipal Council. Therefore, this matter can be considered at a later date. This opinion was recorded in the minutes of the meeting. The minutes were submitted to the board of directors on the 18th and approved for record after some discussion.

Request for Price Increase 122

The Shanghai Telephone Company sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council on August 15th of this year requesting a price increase. The main points of the original letter were released by the Shanghai Municipal Council Information Office yesterday. The following is a summary: The Shanghai Telephone Company took over the former company in 1930 and immediately began converting to automatic switchboards. This work was completed within the concession on March 26th of last year. Since that date, telephone charges have been increased separately based on Anson's report. The company sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council on August 5th, 1930, stating that the company would not request a price increase within three years of the implementation of Anson's prices. However, the situation has changed greatly since August 1930.

Because the exchange rate calculated by Anson was 61.839 US dollars per 100 taels of silver, while the average in the company's accounts was only 32.901 US dollars per 100 taels, the cost increased significantly, and the amount of income was not sufficient to be profitable. Under these circumstances, the letter of August 5th, 1930, cannot be strictly interpreted, and the Shanghai Municipal Council must be asked to consider it.

Benefits Obtained by Users Throughout the City 123

The period for converting to automatic switchboards was originally set at two years, but it was actually completed in only 599 days. Furthermore, the number of calls since the conversion to automatic switchboards has approximately doubled, compared to the estimate as of the end of May 1933, which was

133. Since users have increased convenience in these several aspects, it does not seem appropriate for the company to bear the losses alone.

Difficult Financial Situation of the Company 124

The company has been losing money ever since the takeover. It lost a total of 270,028 taels from August 1930 to March 1932, and 72,000 taels from April 1932 to May 1933. Dividends have not been distributed to shareholders, and reserves cannot be allocated. If prices are not increased in the future, the company will lose 167,000 taels per year. The company's costs include 8,796,093 taels for the purchase of the old company and 17,735,452 taels for the new company's expenses up to the end of July 1932, totaling over 26 million taels. Of this, 5,757,100 taels were invested by shareholders, and the rest was paid for with company bonds and loans.

Comparison with Major Cities in Europe and America 125

Telephones in Shanghai make 906 calls per day, which is two to three times more than in some major cities in Europe and America. However, the cost of a call is approximately 2.2 cents in Shanghai for commercial use, while it is 1.16 yuan in Philadelphia, USA. For residential use, it is 2.7 cents in Shanghai and 1.22 yuan in Philadelphia. The installation cost per telephone is over 624 taels in Shanghai, while it is mostly 700 to 800 taels in European and American cities. The

difficulty lies in the fact that the ratio of income to cost is too low.

Extent of Losses Suffered by the Company 126

Taking the 14 months from April 1932 to May 1933 as an example, the net income should have been 3,115,000 taels according to the amount permitted by the contract (i.e., 8% of the investment, plus 2% for reserves). However, the actual net income was only 1,441,000 taels, a shortfall of 1,674,000 taels. This includes 979,000 taels of dividends payable but not paid, 623,000 taels of reserves payable but not paid, and an actual loss of 72,000 taels. The losses suffered by shareholders and reserves are what users have saved.

Request for a Price Increase is Only for Compensation 127

The company is not disregarding the original letter of August 5th, 1930, but only wishes to obtain an income that is lower than what is permitted by the contract within these three years. Since the installation of the automatic switchboards has been completed, it does not seem appropriate to allow the company to continue operating at a loss for so long. Furthermore, shareholders should receive at least a minimum dividend within these three years. As for the reserves, they can be set aside after three years. Therefore, the company's request is to allow a price increase from now until the end of March 1935 (i.e., when the three-year period ends) to generate a revenue of 1,061,000 taels. This number is calculated based on: (1) Compensating for the actual loss of 37,000 taels (expected to be lost by then), and (2) Paying a 4% interest rate for the three-year period on the 5,757,100 taels of paid-in capital, totaling 691,000 taels. If this request is approved by September 20th of this year, it can be implemented on December 1st, in which case the increase should be allocated over 16 months, requiring a price increase of 20.07%. If it is approved by December 20th and implemented on March 1st of next year, it must be allocated over 13 months, requiring a price increase of 24.70%.

The Case of the Confiscation of Hainan Island's Local Sugar; Xing Juefei Scheduled to Go to Peiping to Petition 131

Guangdong sugar merchants held a meeting yesterday to welcome and discuss relief measures. Due to the suspicion that Hainan Island's local sugar was adulterated with foreign sugar, it was repeatedly confiscated and heavily fined by the Qiongzhou Customs, causing great losses to local merchants and farmers. Therefore, representatives, including Xing Juefei, were sent north to appeal to the central government. Details have been reported in previous newspapers. Since the representative arrived in Shanghai, he has announced the matter to all parties and requested assistance from organizations such as the National Federation of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Guangdong Association in Shanghai, and representatives of various counties in South China, including Li Yansheng from Qinlian, Li Wenhua from Huizhou, Zhao Yuanshan from Gaozhou, Wan Minyi from Hainan Island, and Guangdong sugar merchants. All believe that this matter has a great impact on the commerce and livelihood of farmers in South China and have expressed their utmost support in appealing to the central government and ensuring the safety of Hainan sugar exports in the future. It is reported that Representative Xing yesterday also personally presented the details of the Qiongzhou Customs' seizure of Hainan Island's local sugar to Director Wen of the Public Security Bureau, requesting his strong assistance. It is said that after hearing about this matter, Director Wen, considering that the agriculture of his hometown is in the process of recovery and is being devastated, expressed his willingness to provide assistance. The Guangdong sugar merchants of Guang'an Tang, wanting to understand the true situation, specially hosted a banquet at Xinghualou last night, inviting Representative Xing to attend and report on the matter. It is reported that the representative will visit Tang Haian, the superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, again today to request assistance. It is also reported that Representative Xing has scheduled to go to Peiping to petition the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, hoping to achieve the desired outcome.

Chamber of Commerce Sends Telegram to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, Requesting that They Order the Release of Hainan Island Products 132

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, based on a letter from Xing Juefei, the representative of the Hainan Island Sugar Merchants and the Haikou Chamber of Commerce, requesting assistance due to the wanton destruction of local sugar, sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Customs Administration, requesting that they order the release of local sugar and prevent further obstruction in the future. The original telegram is excerpted below (titles omitted): "Recently, we received a letter from Xing Juefei, the representative of the Hainan Island Sugar Merchants and the Haikou Chamber of Commerce, stating that (details omitted, as seen in the 18th issue of the newspaper). Respectfully presented by Lin, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, etc., based on this, we have found that currently, only the Fujian and Guangdong provinces produce sugar in our country, and Hainan Island produces the most. If we do not take measures to promote it and allow it to be destroyed, domestic sugar will disappear from the market and we will consume only foreign sugar. The Qionghai Customs has created difficulties in the past, and the Jianghai Customs is now auctioning goods, which is a major blow to domestic sugar. We hereby telegraph to your ministry for review and approval, earnestly requesting that you quickly order the Qiongjiang Customs to release the seized local sugar, return the collected fines, and prevent intentional obstruction of local sugar exports in the future, in order to maintain domestic production. Respectfully, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce."

The Industrial Circle of This City is Planning Proposals for the National Production Conference, Focusing on Centralized Organization, Expanding the Quantity of Raw Materials, Promoting Production and Sales Cooperation, and Relieving Industrial Finance 133

Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo, in view of the declining domestic production, has decided to hold a National Production Conference in Hangzhou on the first of next month to discuss relief measures. The industrial circle of this city is currently planning all the proposals to be submitted to the conference for discussion. The Central News Agency reporter inquired about the situation from the industrial circle of this city yesterday, and the information obtained is as follows.

Motivation for Convening the Conference 134

Since the September 18th Incident, the status of China's industrial production has undergone tremendous changes. Under such circumstances, if no concrete measures are taken to remedy the situation, not only will the existing production be on the verge of extinction, but the emerging industries will find it even more difficult to establish themselves. In December of the 21st year of the Republic of China, during the plenary session, representatives from the industrial circle of this city, who were all gathered in Shanghai, presented the difficulties of the industry. They received instructions to convene a production conference independently under the guidance of the government. At the same time, the government also opened up and used the strength of all parties to enable the resolutions of the conference to be realized through political power. The process of the negotiations at that time was to draft a proposal for convening a production conference, which was considered satisfactory by Committee Member Wu and others, who personally revised it. It was submitted to the Third Plenary Session on December 10, 21st year of the Republic of China and was passed in full on December 19th of the same month. It was handed over to the Executive Yuan to instruct the competent authorities to handle it. This is the general situation of the motivation for the production conference at that time.

General Decline in Production 135

In recent years, the decline in domestic production has been such that not only are the industrial raw materials required by the general large industries in the country purchased from abroad, but also the agricultural raw materials such as wheat and cotton, which are used to manufacture cotton yarn and flour, are mostly imported from foreign countries. For example, the national cotton production is estimated at more than 6.4 million piculs per year, while in the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the Chinese cotton production was 6,793,241 piculs, and the import of American cotton reached 4,652,726 piculs. The national wheat production is 8 million piculs per year, while in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the import of foreign wheat reached 22,773,424 piculs, valued at Customs Silver 7,639,301 taels. The trend will only increase in the future. Other industrial raw materials, such as phosphorus for matches, nitric acid soda for bleaching and dyeing, pigments for printing and dyeing, woolen yarn for knitting, and tobacco leaves for cigarettes, are imported annually, valued at over 300 million taels of Customs Silver. Various procedures for exploring and paying prices are affected by fluctuations in foreign exchange rates and are also subject to foreign commercial trusts.

Under the current situation, China is still a producing country. If it can actively reorganize and strive for progress, starting with the four items of cotton, wheat, wool, and tobacco leaves, it is not impossible to achieve self-sufficiency and alleviate a portion of the economic pressure. The import of cotton accounts for the top position of customs imports, and China's cotton land is as much as 35,468,352 mu, ranking second in the world in cotton production. The area north of the Yellow River and west of Huaihai is the center of wheat production, with an area of over 485 million mu. Furthermore, Sichuan and Shandong provinces produce a large amount of tobacco, and wool is a special product of northern Hebei. As long as breeding is improved and incentives are provided, it may not be necessary to rely on foreign goods in two or three years.

Improving the Freight System 136

To alleviate the decline in production, in addition to encouraging production, the freight system should be improved first. In countries with developed production, the three items of production, transportation, and sales are connected and consistent. From production to transportation to sales, each item has an independent organization, and then each organization is merged into a single general organization for operation. With strong strength and low consumption, goods can reduce prices and compete with overseas goods. The wealth of the country will also increase accordingly. On the other hand, in China, agricultural products cannot raise prices due to the lack of transit agents. Factory products are immediately owned by merchants because there is no industrial specialized transportation agency. Over time, transportation agents have to rely on customs brokers and transit companies to perform their labor. The impact is that not only is the price of goods in the producing and selling areas far apart, but also the hub of national production and transit is controlled by middlemen. The connection between production and sales is cut off, and the purchasing power of users is reduced accordingly. The direct and indirect intangible consumption can brew a fundamental crisis in national production. For now, the only way is for the government to plan for the industrial circle and order the investment organization to run a large-scale industrial transit company within a short period of time, and to detail the company's business and management rules. At the same time, it will also order local customs and railways to set up special commercial cargo transit points, so that all goods can be picked up, transported, and dispatched upon arrival. In addition, it will encourage domestic banks to provide more mortgages for such cargo transportation, providing practical double convenience. In this way, at the same time

By communicating between the production and sales sides, the price of goods will naturally be cheaper, and purchasing power will be strengthened, preventing the stagnation of goods. The domestic and foreign markets will also be opened up by this.

Proposals Are Being Drafted 137

The National Production Conference is scheduled to be held in Hangzhou on the first of next month. Industrial circles in various places are currently recommending representatives and drafting proposals to be submitted to the conference for discussion. The industrial circle of this city is discussing the candidates for representatives and proposals. The general ideas of the proposals include the following points: (1) Systematically merge and centralize various existing investigation and agricultural planting agencies and groups in China to expand the quantity of raw material production. (2) Cooperate with the financial sector to organize industrial transportation agencies. (3) Promote production and sales cooperation, so that the domestic market is gradually dominated by domestic goods. (4) Generate a center of gravity for industrial organizations and ask the government to formulate separate industrial group organization laws. (5) Revise industrial and commercial laws and regulations, and abolish those that are not practical. (6) Relieve industrial finance and advocate that financial institutions use at least a certain percentage of cash each year for industrial purposes.

Brigadier General Who Shines Shoes, Jiang Minsheng, Develops a New Way to Save the Country; The Dahua Pencil Factory Entrusts Him to Sell 30,000 Pencils; 30% of the Profits Will Be Used as a Fund to Aid Northeastern Refugees; Jiang Minsheng Organizes a Planning Group to Address the Livelihood Problems of Northeastern Refugees 153

Anti-Japanese General Jiang Minsheng, wandering at sea and shining shoes to make a living, caused a sensation. Newspapers competed to report on his whereabouts. He also published his monthly income in full, and the surplus was sent to the Shanghai charitable organizations within the United Federation for the Relief of Northeastern Refugees to relieve Northeastern compatriots. Although it was a drop in the bucket, it won the sympathy of patriots in society. The Dahua Pencil Factory in this city had previously donated 240 dozen pencils, instructing him to sell them, which was quite successful, and the proceeds were also donated to aid Northeastern compatriots. Dahua recently sent another letter to Mr. Jiang.

Dahua's Original Letter 154

Mr. Minsheng, Northeast is unfortunate and is invaded by the Japanese, causing the 30 million compatriots in the Northeast to be in dire straits. Your anti-Japanese spirit is admired by the whole country. All affected compatriots should be assisted as much as possible. The factory has this purpose and has discussed with you several times. Now, it is approved to entrust you to lead the affected compatriots to various places to sell 30,000 pencils of the factory's products, totaling 126,000 yuan. In the future, 30% of the sales proceeds, totaling 37,800 yuan, will be used as a fund to fundamentally aid the affected Northeastern compatriots and for the expenses required for sales. Although it is a drop in the bucket, it is also a way to help and the obligation that compatriots should fulfill. I hereby announce this and wish you well. Wu Zhongshan.

Request for Supervision 155

Mr. Jiang Minsheng, upon receiving this letter, felt that the factory's enthusiasm for public welfare and the current urgency for relief for the Northeastern compatriots seemed to make him able to take on the responsibility of sales. However, the number was too large, and he was deeply worried about any mistakes. He sent a letter to the Shanghai charitable organizations, the United Federation for the Relief of Northeastern Refugees, requesting that someone be sent to supervise in order to show good faith. On October 7th, he received a reply from the association, "In response, we received a letter stating that Manager Wu Zhongshan of the Dahua Pencil Factory in Shanghai is willing to entrust you with the sales of 30,000 pencils of the factory's products, and to take 30% of the proceeds for the relief of Northeastern refugees. You asked this association to send someone to supervise it for the sake of trustworthiness, showing modesty and humility. We are very appreciative of your reputation for trustworthiness. From past events, it is deeply admired by colleagues, and there is no need to send anyone. We hereby reply in a corresponding letter, hoping for your review and compliance." Mr. Jiang Minsheng, with righteousness in mind, cannot shirk his responsibility. However, the matter is too complicated, and he is sincerely afraid that the wrong person will be entrusted, or that his credibility will be undermined. He is currently recruiting capable young people from the Northeastern refugees who have difficult and hard lives to first organize a "Planning Group to Address the Livelihood Problems of Northeastern Refugees." Mr. Jiang will lead the group members to carry out a pilot sales plan. On the one hand, in Peiping, Tianjin, and other places, members of the group will be assigned to sell separately, and the proceeds will be delivered to the Shanghai charitable organizations at any time to the United Federation for the Relief of Northeastern Refugees for proper management, in order to relieve Northeastern refugees.

Recently, as the weather has become cooler, the western district has become desolate. It has been determined that Qiu and Jiang committed more than eleven roadside robberies from December 8th of last year until their arrest. Therefore, there was not enough time for questioning this morning, and he requested an adjournment for a special hearing.
