Gu Desheng Unexpectedly Fails to Qualify Wan-Meter Exhibition Kim Jung-Kang Wins 36 Minutes and 1 Second Result Was Disappointing Wang Zheng-Lin Second and Wang Hui-Bin Third 215

Overwhelming Spectacle in Nanjing Attended by 50,000 216

(Nanjing, 19th dispatch) At 2:30 PM on the 19th, the 10,000-meter exhibition race began. Five participants included Jin Gudesheng, Wang Huibin, Chen Shusen of Shanghai, Wang Zhenglin, and Su Jinzhongkang. At the start, Gu led, followed by Wang, Chen third, Wang fourth, and Jin in last place.

No Change 217

There was no change from the first to the fifth lap. In the sixth, seventh, and eighth laps, Jin Zhongkang chased up, with Wang Zhenglin remaining in fourth place. In the ninth lap, Jin briefly surged ahead but soon fell back to fourth. There were no changes in the tenth, eleventh, and twelfth laps. However, Wang Zhenglin was very close, conserving his strength for the final sprint. In the thirteenth lap, Jin's attempt to surge failed and was overcome by Wang Huibin, who took the lead. Jin remained in fourth place, and Gu Desheng fell back to second.

Mid-Race Scenario 218

No change in the fourteenth lap. In the fifteenth and sixteenth laps, Gu moved forward again, with Jin still in fourth and Wang Zhenglin at the rear. By the seventeenth lap, Jin gradually showed his strength, surging to second place, forming a lineup of Gu, Jin, Wang Chen and Wang Zhenglin. By the eighteenth lap, Gu still led, about twenty meters ahead of Jin. Wang Huibin was behind Jin, and Wang Zhenglin of Shanghai remained at the rear, conserving energy for the sprint. By the nineteenth lap, the final stage had arrived. Jin sprinted with all his might, surging ahead of Gu by several meters.

Final Half Lap 219

In the final half lap, Jin fought even harder, eventually outpacing Gu by over twenty meters to win the championship. Gu looked pale, showing signs of exhaustion, and ultimately failed to qualify, which was quite unexpected. Jin's expression remained unchanged. In the final half lap, he had already secured first place, finishing in 36 minutes and 1 second. Wang Zhenglin of Shanghai sprinted with all his might in the final lap, finishing only four or five meters behind Jin, proving his reputation as a great general was well-deserved. Wang Huibin of Jin came third, Chen Shusen of Jin fourth, and Gu Desheng fifth.

Sensation in Nanjing 220

The 10,000-meter exhibition drew national attention. Nearly 50,000 spectators attended. Taxis in Nanjing were fully booked. Key figures of the National Government, including Shao Yuanchong, Wu Tiecheng, and Zhu Jiahua, arrived before 2 PM. Upon completion of the race, the audience applauded continuously for as long as ten minutes. The Jiangsu team waved their hats and cheered joyously. Zhu Jiahua particularly expressed his respect for Jin. Jin even went to the Eastern rostrum to meet the key figures before departing. A previously unresolvable public case was thus settled. Those who praised Gu turned to praise Jin. Su Jin's name will be widely known in this era.

A Farewell Letter from Athletes of the Five Northeastern Provinces One Word, One Tear, Unbearable to Finish Reading 221

▲ Ardently Hoping and Sincerely Praying

▲ Next National Games to Be Held at the Shenyang Sports Field

▲ The Overall Championship is to Restore the Colors of the Northeast

Fellow comrades and compatriots, the Games have closed, and everyone has returned home. We, however, continue to drift. For us, these ten days were like a reprieve from a shipwreck, a chance to see our homeland again, to reunite with our siblings, an immeasurable blessing. Therefore, every blade of grass and tree here seems to hold infinite affection for us. Every word and smile from you all seems to carry deep meaning for us. Truly, your handshakes have healed much of our shattered spirit, and your applause has strengthened our will to fight. We truly hate to part, but the nation needs each of you to work hard. Life itself can be sacrificed, so what is separation? Goodbye, everyone. The autumn winds are harsh, take care, take care.

The spoils of victory that you take back are either five-foot golden spears or championship silver shields. Guess what treasures we are taking back? "Hope" and "Confidence." Seeing your spirit of teamwork and the vigorous strength of your bodies, we are indeed confident that China has hope. Therefore, we hope that the team spirit displayed on this athletic field can spread to all sectors and can revitalize the strength of the nation. We not only hope that land will not be lost again but also that we can reclaim our beautiful land. Looking at the amazing records that you have created, we increasingly believe that anything others can do, we can also do. As the saying goes, "He is a man, and I am a man; whoever acts can be so." It only lies in one's own efforts. If the Japanese can destroy a country, can't we restore it? Therefore, the souvenirs we bring back from the athletic field are the beliefs that "With you, the Northeast will not fall" and "With you, the Northeast will surely be strong." As for ourselves, we will of course stand on the front lines and work hard.

Goodbye, everyone. In a single word of farewell, you have given us these precious souvenirs - hope and confidence. How grateful we are! How can we repay you? All we have are the scars left behind by painful experiences, awareness, and recognition to give to you. We realize that before today, the path that Chinese youth were accustomed to taking was completely wrong: shouting slogans, pasting posters, talking about revolution while neglecting the nation, discussing national salvation while abandoning scholarship. After all, it cannot stop planned aggression or resist wars with national characteristics. We, from top to bottom, each looked after our own interests and sought our own benefits, so that in the end, when the skin is gone, what can the fur adhere to? Only perishing together. Our only way out from now on is to bury ourselves in hard work, endure hardship, and train hard. In a word, be foolishly diligent.

Our second scar is recognizing our own responsibilities. In talking about national disasters, it is always good to blame a few individuals or a certain political party. In fact, apart from the good people who work diligently all day long, who does not bear a considerable responsibility? We, scattered north and south, often hear voices of complaint and blame, and rarely see warriors who fulfill their responsibilities and say, "If not me, who?" More often, credit is claimed for oneself, and blame is shifted to others. National grievances can be ignored, but private hatreds cannot be left unavenged. Wrong practices become the norm. Even if the Japanese do not come to destroy us, how can we be spared? As Nelson famously said, "England expects that every man will do his duty." Today, China truly needs everyone to do their duty. We must have this awareness to transform ourselves and to revive the nation.

Our awareness and recognition are gained from the nation's unprecedented sacrifices and our own immense suffering. The price is too high. We give them to you to take back, to share with everyone, and to advise them not to pay the same price. Alas, the taste of national subjugation is truly not to be tried. Originally, the civilization, barbarism, rise, and fall of a nation all depend on whether they can exchange experiences. The disasters we have suffered, we hope, will be sufficient for our compatriots to learn from. If all the youth of the country can recognize their responsibilities, our hope will surely be fulfilled.

Our confidence will surely be realized. Finally, we ardently hope and sincerely pray that the next National Games of the Republic of China will be held at the Shenyang Beiling Sports Field and that the overall championship of the next National Games of the Republic of China will be to restore the colors of the Northeast. We have come this time and received the sympathy and assistance of the government authorities and compatriots from all walks of life. We would like to take this opportunity to express our sincere thanks on behalf of ourselves and the Northeast Sports Promotion Association. Dare to salute, athletes from the five provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Jehol, and Harbin, Nanjing, October 20, 1933.

My Thoughts on the National Games 222

— Liu Xuesong

This year's National Games was held in Nanking. I was fortunate to participate in the event and have many observations. Thinking back to last year in America, the enthusiastic atmosphere of welcoming our country's delegation to the World Games, another year has passed without realizing it. Considering the reasons for Europe and America's progress and our country's decline, there are two main reasons: one is the lack of promotion from above, and the other is the lack of effort from below. However, apart from this, the lack of magnificent and complete sports venues also consistently hinders the popularization and development of sports. This time, the central government spent 1.3 to 1.4 million to build the National Games venue, including track and field, swimming pools, basketball courts, martial arts arenas, etc., all of which are extremely magnificent. The excellent facilities not only aid sports but also show the hard work of those above in promoting them. On the athlete's side, more than 2,000 athletes gathered from the north and south, with full spirits and serious attitudes. The records of each event have shown excellent progress, which is also greatly different from the past. This is truly gratifying. The referees were cautious in enforcing the rules, all of them being well-informed and experienced individuals in the country, which is truly admirable. It is hoped that the athletes can uphold the spirit of sportsmanship, not focusing on wins and losses, so that the Games can end completely without any disputes. In terms of venue layout, it was also very perfect due to the hard work of the organizers. Although there were some improper arrangements in the reception, with so many people and complicated matters, the representatives had to be understanding. As for the public, participation was also very enthusiastic. Compared to those who were indifferent to sports in the past, this has also changed drastically. This is also sufficient evidence of our country's achievements in promoting sports in recent years. If the National Games can be held annually, then the future progress of sports can be predicted.

Central China Sports Promotion Association First Executive Committee Meeting Recommends the Fifth Central China Games Be Held in Hankou Next April 225

The first executive committee meeting of the Central China Sports Promotion Association was held at the Central Hotel at 7:30 PM on the 18th. Song Ruhai, Yuan Jun, Wang (Wu Zhongjun deputizing), Huang Fengqi (He Jingwei deputizing), Gong Zhenfan attended, with Yuan Jun presiding. The following matters were resolved: (1) The official seal of the association was determined. It was resolved that the seal of the association would be named "Seal of the Central China Sports Promotion Association," made of wood, 1.5 inches square. (2) How should membership fees be collected? It was resolved that the executive members of each province would be responsible for collecting them and remit them to the chief executive member Yuan Jun by November of this year. (3) How should the work of the association be carried out? It was resolved that: 1. It is recommended that the board of directors request the fifth Central China Games to be held in Hubei in April 1934. 2. It is recommended that the education authorities of each province hold a ten-mile cross-country race before the end of December of this year and report the results to the association. 3. Starting from New Year's Day 1934, the Central China Basketball Competition will be held in Hubei (the venue and dormitory will be the responsibility of the executive member of the competition site, and all expenses for preparation will be borne by each unit). However, the number of players on each team is limited to ten. 4. It is recommended that the board of directors request each provincial department of education to subsidize the association's annual operating expenses by 100 yuan.

Second National Martial Arts Examination to Open This Morning in Beijing; Session to Last Seven Days 228

(Nanjing, 19th) The second National Martial Arts Examination is scheduled to open on the 20th in the morning, with performances beginning in the afternoon. More than 400 contestants from various provinces and cities have arrived for the examination, which will last for seven days. The schedule is as follows:

* National Martial Arts Examination: 1:30 PM on the 20th, national physical education performance, preliminary testing of boxing.

* 21st: Preliminary testing of boxing.

* 22nd Morning: Formal testing, boxing competition.

* 23rd Morning: Short weapons competition, Afternoon: Long weapons competition.

* 24th Morning: Free sparring competition, Afternoon: Wrestling competition.

* 25th Morning: Boxing finals, Afternoon: Weapons finals.

* 26th Morning: Free sparring finals, Afternoon: Wrestling finals.

* 27th Morning: Saber splitting, spear thrusting, Afternoon: Examination of academic subjects; items: Party Principles, Martial Arts Origins, Chinese Language.

Examinations will begin every day in both the morning and afternoon. Chiang Kai-shek and He Jian both sent telegrams to Beijing to express their congratulations on the second National Martial Arts Examination. Chiang Kai-shek also sent Cao Haosen as a military representative to participate.

▲Examination Regulations

The National Martial Arts Examination will be held in Beijing today. The regulations for the National Martial Arts Examination are as follows:

Article 1: The National Martial Arts Examination is divided into three levels: A. National Examination, B. Provincial (Municipal) Examination, C. County Examination.

Article 2: Organization of Examinations at Each Level: A. National Examination: The Central Martial Arts Academy will submit a report to the National Government, which will organize an Examination Committee in accordance with the established National Examination date. B. Provincial (Municipal) Examination: In accordance with the established Provincial (Municipal) Examination date, the Provincial (Municipal) Government, together with the Provincial (Municipal) Martial Arts Academy, will organize an Examination Committee. C. County Examination: In accordance with the established County Examination date, the County Government, together with the County Martial Arts Academy, will organize an Examination Committee.

Article 3: Examination Qualifications: A. County Examination: Any citizen of the Republic of China recommended by the village head, etc., may participate in the examination. B. Provincial (Municipal) Examination: Only those selected by the County Examination and recommended by the County Government may participate in the examination. C. National Examination: Only those selected by the Provincial (Municipal) Examination and recommended by the Provincial (Municipal) Government may participate in the examination. D. Those proficient in martial arts currently serving in various institutions, not returning to their place of origin, but volunteering to take the examination, must be recommended by their respective governing institutions and deemed qualified by the respective Examination Committees before they can participate in any level of examination. E. Traveling expenses for examinees shall be issued by the recommending institution, taking into account the distance of the journey.

Article 4: The Number of Passing Candidates is as follows: A. Those who pass the County Examination will be given certificates by the County Government, with a maximum of three to ten passing candidates. B. Those who pass the Provincial (Municipal) Examination will be given certificates by the Provincial (Municipal) Government according to their grade, with a maximum of ten to forty passing candidates for the Provincial Examination and five to fifteen for the Municipal Examination. C. The National Examination will be issued certificates by the Central Martial Arts Academy, with the number of candidates as follows: (1) First Class: Three candidates; (2) Second Class: Twenty to thirty candidates; (3) Third Class: Fifty to one hundred and twenty candidates.

Article 5: Reporting the Number of Candidates: A. National Examination: Each province (city) must submit the list of examinees to the Academy two months before the National Examination for statistics, allocation, and the dates of the preliminary and formal examinations. B. Provincial (Municipal) Examination: Each county must submit the number of candidates for the Provincial (Municipal) Examination to the Provincial (Municipal) Martial Arts Academy two months before the Provincial (Municipal) Examination for statistics, allocation, and the dates of the preliminary and formal examinations. C. County Examination: Each district, village, and community must submit the number of candidates for the County Examination one month before the County Examination for statistics, allocation, and the dates of the preliminary and formal examinations.

Article 6: Examination Dates: A. National Examination: Scheduled for the month of October each year. B. Provincial (Municipal) Examination: Scheduled for the month of April each year. C. County Examination: Scheduled for the month of December each year.

Article 7: Examination Subjects: A. Practical Skills: (1) Boxing, (2) Weapons (Spear, Saber, Sword, Staff), (3) Wrestling, (4) Free Sparring, (5) Saber Splitting, (6) Spear Thrusting. B. Academic Subjects: (1) Party Principles, (2) Chinese Language, (3) Geography, (4) History, (5) Martial Arts Origins, (6) Physiology and Hygiene.

Article 8: Examination Method: Divided into preliminary and formal examinations. Preliminary Examination: A. National Examination: Preliminary examination subjects: Boxing, Weapons (Spear, Saber, Sword, Staff), Wrestling, Free Sparring, Saber Splitting, Spear Thrusting. Candidates who can test in two or more items are considered qualified. Those who fail the preliminary examination may not participate in the formal examination. B. Provincial (Municipal) Examination: Preliminary examination is the same as the National Examination. C. County Examination: Preliminary examination is the same as the Provincial (Municipal) Examination. Formal Examination: A. National Examination: (1) Preliminary Test: Uses the weight division grouping method, with an elimination system, to test boxing, weapons, wrestling, free sparring, saber splitting, and spear thrusting. Those who can test in two or more items are considered qualified, and are selected up to the original number of Third Class candidates. (2) Retest: Still uses the method of the preliminary test. Those selected as Third Class candidates will compete against each other, selecting up to the original number of Second Class candidates. (3) Final Test: Still uses the method of the preliminary test. Those selected as Second Class candidates will compete against each other, selecting the top three First Class candidates. B. Provincial (Municipal) Examination: The method and subjects of the preliminary test, retest, and final test are the same as the National Examination. Candidates are also divided into First, Second, and Third Class according to the quota. C. County Examination: The method and subjects of the preliminary test, retest, and final test are the same as the Provincial and Municipal Examinations. Candidates are also divided into First, Second, and Third Class according to the quota.

Article 9: Weight Division Grouping Method: A. Examinees will be divided into five weight classes according to their body weight (the details of the weight classes are in the detailed rules of the National Martial Arts Examination). B. Candidates in each weight class will be divided into five groups, and a roster will be prepared, filled in according to the order. C. All candidates who have been called by name in each weight class should gather at the designated location and wait quietly for the examination and must not leave without permission. D. The Chief Judge will designate judges to call names by grade and conduct the competition in order.

Article 10: Appointment of Chief Judge: A. The Chief Judge of the National Examination will be appointed by the National Examination Committee from martial arts experts or education experts. B. The Chief Judge of the Provincial/Municipal Examination will be appointed by the Provincial/Municipal Examination Committee from martial arts experts or education experts. C. The Chief Judge of the County Examination will be appointed by the County Examination Committee from martial arts experts or education experts.

Article 11: Detailed Rules for the National Martial Arts Examination will be determined separately by the Central Martial Arts Academy.

Article 12: The standards for judging shall be handled in accordance with the detailed rules of the National Martial Arts Examination.

Article 13: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they shall be amended by the Central Martial Arts Academy at any time.

Article 14: These regulations shall be formulated by the Central Martial Arts Academy, submitted to the Examination Yuan of the National Government for record, and promulgated for implementation.

Telegrams of Congratulations from Chiang and He 229

(Nanjing, 19th) The second National Martial Arts Examination will open on the morning of the 20th. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and Commander-in-Chief He Xilu both sent telegrams to Beijing to express their congratulations on the National Examination. The telegrams are recorded separately as follows: (1) Telegram to Director Zhang Zhen of the Central Martial Arts Academy: I have learned that I have been recommended as the Honorary Chairman of the Second National Martial Arts Examination. This matter concerns the revitalization of the national spirit and I will certainly strive to undertake it. However, I am currently busy with the suppression campaign and cannot attend the meeting. I have telegraphed Vice Minister Cao of the Ministry of Military Affairs to attend on my behalf. Secret, Chiang Kai-shek. (2) Telegram to Mr. Zhang Zimin, Director of the Central Martial Arts Academy: I have respectfully received your telegram. Martial arts are the foundation for strengthening the race and saving the country. The Central Government is holding this examination this time, and I deeply admire its enthusiastic promotion. I very much wanted to participate in the grand ceremony and also planned to go to Nanchang and then to Beijing to receive your instruction. However, due to the arrangement of the suppression campaign, I was unable to start the journey. I am deeply sorry. I have now sent Chief Captain Li Lijiuchao to Secretary Kairan, leading the staff to Beijing for reference. I would be grateful for your guidance. Respectfully, He Jian.

This inspection is different from previous ones. All schools must be inspected in detail, and much guidance must be given on education administration. For secondary schools, emphasis is placed on vocational and teacher training education.

A. Regarding the Ministry's Outline of Service and Treatment Methods for Faculty and Staff of Secondary Schools and the Department's Interim Regulations on the Appointment, Employment, Dismissal, and Treatment of Principals and Staff of Secondary Schools: 1. What is the effect of implementing the integration of teaching and discipline? 2. What are the standards for selecting class directors? What are the advantages and disadvantages of renewing teacher appointments for one academic year versus two academic years?

Is it necessary to have an administrative director for vocational schools with few classes? 3. Is it convenient to submit documents for teacher qualification review one month before the start of school? Are there any difficulties?

Are there any difficulties in each school? (Please provide the average income and expenditure of miscellaneous fees in the last three years, as well as the expenditure of library and sports fees, and state whether there has been any misappropriation, and for what purpose.) 7. What are the opinions of each school on the allocation of various regular accounting items? 8. In addition to the current committees for discipline, financial audit, and vocational guidance and promotion, should the existing fees of other committees in each school actually exist?

D. Regarding the Ministry's Interim Regulations on the Secondary School Graduation Examination: 1. How should the dates of the formal examination and the retest be arranged to make it convenient for both the examination office and the students? 2. Do the achievements of the students who passed and failed the two graduation examinations match their achievements in school during the three years? Are there any major differences? (Please list the names and compare the school grades and the examination grades for future reference.) 3. The reasons for the poor performance of students in the two graduation examinations in each subject and the remedies. 4. Opinions on the questions of the two graduation examinations. 5. Opinions on the examination procedures and the method of calculating grades. 6. How does the examination affect regular teaching?

E. Regarding the Department's Organizational Outline for Subject Teaching Research Associations in Secondary Schools: 1. What was the actual situation of each school organizing subject teaching research associations in the 21st year? 2. How can each school encourage teachers of each subject to increase research interest and improve teaching efficiency? 3. How can each school promote the continued learning of teachers of each subject? 4. How should the research results be published and reported so that they can be jointly studied?

F. Other: 1. Does each school have special facilities and plans for national defense education? How is it implemented? 2. Does each school have an active plan for guiding students' thoughts and correcting bad habits? 3. Does each school have a plan to add to the equipment of teaching aids such as books, instruments, and specimens year by year? (Please provide a list of the equipment added and the amount of money in the last three years, and it is best to list each item year by year.) How is it kept? 4. What are the concrete opinions of each school on improving the efficiency of military training and intensifying physical training? 7. Other.

Spring and Autumn

Zheng He's Voyages to the West 235

— Yanqiao

Previously, Yongle Emperor sent Zheng He to the South Seas, which added a unique interest to the communication between China and the islands of Southeast Asia. It was still very valuable to increase the understanding of China by Southeast Asians. In my estimation, the long-lasting prevalence of this story has been fueled by the addition of embellishments and exaggerations in folk legends. The vernacular novel "Eunuch Sanbao's Voyages to the West" is not very impactful because its depiction is too unsophisticated, so its influence is minimal.

According to Mr. Xu Yunqiao, who resided in Java and Siam for five years, there are numerous myths about Sanbao in various parts of Southeast Asia, and he is addressed as "Sanbao Gong," with statues erected and temples built to commemorate him. The impression he left is even greater than that of Zhang Qian and Ban Chao in the Western Regions. However, Chinese records of Sanbao, apart from a few pages of simple descriptions of his merits in the History of Ming Eunuchs, are completely devoid of anything else. Colonialism without support is ultimately subject to exclusion, and a grand but impractical pacification policy cannot compare with the well-planned, organized, and resourceful Dutch East India Company. The dispute over the Spratly Islands is truly like losing the bamboo raft and trying to salvage the "firecracker" pole.

Wang Risheng's Taiwan Waiji (Outer History of Taiwan) states that Yongle Emperor sent eunuch Wang Sanbao to the Western Seas, combining Zheng He's childhood name with his companion Wang Jingxian's surname. He also says that the Dutch asked Sanbao for blueprints of seagoing vessels, but Sanbao, fearing that they would use the ships to harass the borders, deliberately used a broken brush to draw a flat circle with two or three vertical sections from end to end in the middle, then splayed the brush bristles and made random strokes. The Dutch copied it accordingly, installing a rope for tracking like all the brush bristles, resulting in a ship that was actually sturdier than the Chinese seagoing vessels. This legend is extremely naive, and those with even a slight knowledge of Dutch colonial history would probably laugh at it. However, it is true that Zheng Chenggong drove out the Dutch and occupied Taiwan because he was threatened by Qing soldiers. This is written vividly and with much detail.

The History of Ming spells "Sanbao" as "Sanbao," but both novels and Southeast Asian historical records spell it as "Sanbao." This is inconsequential. However, it is laughable to conflate Southeast Asia with the West. This is due to the era, and cannot be deeply blamed. Chinese people only know that Mount Putuo is in the South Seas, so naturally the idea of the abundant Southeast Asia never occurred to them.

Meeting Room 236

— Yun Sun

Reception rooms, waiting rooms, and meeting rooms are all places to receive guests. Some are not called rooms but halls, which implies a larger scope in terms of definition. We know that a meeting room can be analyzed for many qualities: mysterious, open, sweet, or bitter. In a meeting room, all sorts of tragic and joyful dramas of separation and reunion can be performed! Colorful dramas of joy, anger, sorrow, and pleasure can be performed! For every organization or group, the meeting room is a central element, and the hosts of the organization or group must put effort into its management. According to the nature of the organization, they arrange the room with elaborate decorations. Closer guests are invited into the host's office, like the "signing room" in old officialdom.

For example, in a school, there would be slogans like "Love, Sincerity, Excellence, and Perseverance" or "Wisdom, Benevolence, and Courage." Enlarged photographs of the principal and graduation photos of students would be decorative elements. Gleaming silver trophies and vases, the more dazzling, the more they demonstrate excellent athletic achievements, with a constant metabolism of athletes. Glass-framed inscriptions from important figures of the Party and state would indicate the numerous awards they have received. Tragic and joyful dramas of separation and reunion also take place in the school's meeting room. The sadness of lovers parting as one goes off to study, cherishing each other and saying goodbye. The joy of Saturdays and Sundays, the school's usual visiting hours. They are originally performing the tragedy of "a day apart feels like three autumns," but are now joyfully reunited and naturally filled with boundless joy: watching movies, eating Western food, and all the unspoken things in between. As for separation and reunion, they can also imagine it in the meeting room. They hate to meet too little! Why part after one night? Longing deepens! Unexpectedly encountering each other fills them with joy? These are the kinds of situations. I once heard of a desperate man who went to see his lover at a girls' school. The gatekeeper pretended to make things difficult, demanding a bribe. The desperate man understood and quietly placed a five-yuan bill under the teacup. This secret of the meeting room then spread throughout the school.

In officialdom, the higher the rank of the person, the more difficult it is to get an audience. Their meeting rooms invariably have two orderlies, or servants who are ruthless exploiters, who use their power to manipulate the guests. When many guests seek an audience with an important figure, they are generally received in the order of their calling cards. If you don't give the servant some small favor, he will turn your card upside down. When the important person's visiting time is over, they will wave their sleeves and leave. What are the joys, angers, sorrows, and pleasures in this? You can understand it just by looking at the guest's face as they leave the yamen. If Director XX or Chairman XX invites this guest to their office, the guest will boast to everyone they meet that Director XX or Chairman XX showed them special favor. In fact, from ancient times to the present, the face of a superior has never been pleasant to look at, so it's no wonder that Tao Yuanming indignantly said, "I will not bow for five pecks of rice."

Crying 237

— Bo Guang

"A man does not shed tears lightly." This saying means that a man's tears will not "wet his blue gown sleeves" unless he can no longer bear it.

But it is not the same for women. Crying is their specialty, so when someone dies in a family, they always find a few women who are good at crying to guard the mourning tent. When they see a guest coming to offer condolences, they start sobbing. After the guest has paid their respects, they immediately stop crying and start talking and laughing. Is there any sadness lingering in their hearts?

Even more so, when a daughter is about to get married, the wedding sedan is at the door, but the bride is sobbing, unwilling to leave her family home. But when she returns home three days after the wedding, she is talking and laughing again. At that time, I don't know whether the bride's heart is sad or happy?

And when a couple quarrels over some trivial matter, and the man strongly refutes her a few times, she can only cry, to soften you men, or else she will play the tricks of crying, starving, and hanging herself, frightening you into running away! These cries are all hypocritical cries.

When a child doesn't get their way, they will cry, and you will give in to them. They know that crying has such great power, so they use crying as blackmail!

So I think it is really not easy to make a man's "tears wet his blue gown sleeves." Except for a few men who shed tears of longing when their parents abandon them, or a handful of tears of farewell when lovers part, I have never seen a man cry loudly. So some cries are all hypocritical cries!

Changes in the European and American Novel World 238

— Yan

Speaking of Edgar Wallace

In recent years, the best harvests in the European and American novel world that have won the praise of audiences are no longer those works that specialize in love and teach people how to flirt, but rather stimulating short detective novels. Among them, the great English novelist Edgar Wallace is the most successful.

The change in audience tastes, needless to say, is influenced by the turbulent situation in the concessions. Anyone with a little insight knows that struggle and striving are the only way out for all people and all groups in the future, so they absolutely don't want to waste their precious time on soft reading materials anymore. What they need is the excitement of hot blood, the sharpening of courage, and the cultivation of bravery. Therefore, Edgar Wallace's "The Four Just Men" has been hailed as the number one work of honor in the British literary world in the past three years because it meets all these conditions.

This book has recently been translated into Chinese by Qin Shouou (sold by China Travel Service in Shanghai and other places). Although I am unwilling to flatter him, I dare to say without hypocrisy that he has not diminished the merits of the original book at all, it is as tense, stimulating, and exciting as the original!

I sincerely hope that this work by an Englishman can awaken the dream of those of us who have no soul, and I hope that in the near future, works full of "the beauty of strength" like this can also appear in our own literary world.

▲Statement: This journal has received a letter from Tao Pianyi of Nanjing, stating that Zhang Yiping's "Official and Wealth," published in this column on October 3, was plagiarized from Tao's "Talking about Officials and Wealth," published in the Central Daily on April 2. After checking, it is confirmed that it was copied in its entirety. In addition to canceling the payment, future submissions will not be published. We hereby declare this.

Spring and Autumn Editorial Department Bai

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 239

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seventeen: Who Can Be Without Emotion? Family Thoughts Discourage the Troops; Soldiers Do Not Suppress Fraud; Bold Words Strengthen the Army

Guan Yaowu has a large family and is burdened enough by his family. But he can't bear to abandon them. Old Tian is an unmarried couple, burning with passion. As for me, I really can't be said to have any relationship between men and women. I shouldn't, shouldn't have been engaged to the Yang family girl on this day. Now that I'm leaving her behind, I can't help but feel a knot in my heart. If I didn't have this engagement with Guizhi, I could come and go freely. Although I still have such an old father, he has always encouraged his son to go to war. He always said, "Raise soldiers for a thousand days, use them for one morning." Even if he is reluctant in his heart, under the current circumstances, it would be somewhat embarrassing to say the word "support," because saying "support" would be making fun of the Yang family girl. After I leave, the Yang family mother and daughter will talk even more behind his back, and it will be even more difficult for him to deal with. Thinking of this, I couldn't help but worry about my old father for a while, and with a disheartened mood, I wanted to go back to the company headquarters to see what Guan Yaowu's attitude was. Thinking this, I soon arrived at Guan's company. Looking inside the door, I saw him lying horizontally in his room, on that small bed, facing upwards, with both legs hanging down from the bed. He had his arms crossed in front of his chest, and I didn't know what he was holding in his hands. His two hands and two index fingers were just spinning incessantly. I laughed and said, "Hey! Old Guan, you're so relaxed." Guan Yaowu turned over and sat up, laughing, "You suddenly said something and scared me." Zhao Ziqiang walked into the room and said, "Where has your mind gone? I said such a lighthearted thing, and you were startled." Guan Yaowu said, "That's right, I'm a lost soul now." Saying that, he chuckled, rubbing his hands together endlessly, showing a troubled expression, wanting to completely vent it out in this rubbing of hands. (217)

Short Story

Madman (Continued) 240

— Mo Yi

In this world, only men spend money to watch female models, no women watch male models. Women, even if they accidentally see a man without pants, are always afraid and run away as if they had seen a big snake. However, tonight is an exception. The women in the alley not only did not run away, but all stood up, craning their necks to look at the man without pants. I was extremely surprised.

"Wooooooo..." The man without pants shouted. "Haha, so many sluts, you want to see? I'm not wearing pants. Ha, ha, ha! Woooooo..."

"Ah, it's him." I couldn't help but exclaim. At the same time, I remembered the scene from a week ago, one night.

That man had only run a few steps towards the alley entrance when he was pulled back by three men; another woman helped him put on his pants.

"No, Xiao Fangzi, I have to find that little rabbit bastard, you can't hold me. Woooooo... Little brother-in-law, evil has its retribution, don't be so ruthless, you know? Get out of the way, you kids, take the horse and find the little rabbit bastard! Woooooo...."

"You three follow him around and come back, don't cause trouble, be careful." That woman said.

So, along with the nosy ones, a total of a dozen people escorted him away.

What is going on? I was just about to go home and ask my wife when I heard a young man next to me ask a woman in her thirties, so I stood and listened.

"I don't know what his surname is, I only hear people call him Kunshan..."

"Kunshan? He must be named Huang. He plays 'flower association'. Huang Kunshan, a tiger." A child blurted out.

"Kunshan was once sick and didn't go on the boat. The more days he stayed at home, the more he heard from friends that his sworn brother was being taken advantage of. At first, he didn't believe it, but after three or four people said it in front of him, he couldn't help but have some doubts in his heart. He sent someone to inquire for a few days, and it was indeed the case. After the man named Zhang came back, he told him everything in detail. He was very angry at the time. Unexpectedly, the woman's rice soup was so effective that the next day, she blamed Kunshan, saying that Kunshan shouldn't ruin her reputation. Kunshan just smiled when he heard this. That woman wouldn't let Kunshan off, and kept telling Zhang that Kunshan wanted to take his place, and that he should give Kunshan's position to her brother as soon as possible, to avoid being attacked by others in the future. Finally, she said that if he didn't believe it, he could inquire everywhere. Zhang inquired and it was indeed the case. In fact, this was all arranged in advance by that woman and her man. So when the last shift of the boat left, there was one less Kunshan on the boat, but one more woman's brother! That is the little brother-in-law that Kunshan was shouting about."

"At that time, Kunshan's illness had not yet recovered, and he was angered by the loss of his job, and the man went crazy. He has been a madman for three or four years now. All day long, he is not given food or drink, and he doesn't eat or drink; when he eats, you give him four or five big bowls, and he can eat them all. He defecates and urinates all over the place, and only his wife (the woman who helped him put on his pants) suffers, it's not a life for a person. Usually, Kunshan doesn't say anything, like a mute. When he thinks of something, he shouts all night. Or he runs outside, saying he is going to catch the little brother-in-law." The three men who just pulled him are all his sons; the money the three of them earn each month is not little, and they are very filial to their father, which shows that good is rewarded with good..."

"Wooooooo... Get out of the way, I've caught the little brother-in-law! Woooooo..."

A dozen people escorted him back.

I watched him enter the door, and two words suddenly appeared on my mind: madman.

Free Talk

Yellow Peril 241

— You Gang

The current so-called "Yellow Peril," we ourselves are referring to the breaching of the Yellow River, but thirty years ago, it was not like that. At that time, it was interpreted as the yellow race about to sweep Europe. Some heroes, upon hearing this, were as pleased as when they were praised by white people as "sleeping lions," and were complacent for several years, preparing to become the masters of Europe. However, the origin of the "Yellow Peril" story is different from what we imagined, it originated with the German Emperor Wilhelm. He also drew a picture, a Roman-dressed warrior, resisting a person coming from the East to the West, but that person was not Confucius, but Buddha. The Chinese were really happy for nothing. So while we were dreaming of the "Yellow Peril," the reality seen by someone in Qingdao under German rule was a poor child who dirtied an electric pole and was picked up by the white patrol, like the Chinese dealing with ducks, and carried upside down.

Now, Hitler's idea of ​​excluding non-Germanic peoples is the same method as the German Emperor.

We no longer dream of the German Emperor's so-called "Yellow Peril," we no longer mention the "sleeping lion," and "vast land and abundant resources, large population" is rarely seen in articles. If it is a lion, it is okay to boast about how fat it is, but if it is a pig or a sheep, being fat is not a good sign. I don't know what we ourselves feel like now?

We seem to no longer think, nor can we find any "symbol." We are watching Haijingbo's wild animal show, appreciating lions and tigers eating beef, and I heard they eat a cow every day. We admire the League of Nations' sanctions against Japan, we despise the League of Nations' inability to sanction Japan; we approve of military reduction to "protect peace," and we also admire Hitler's withdrawal from military reduction; we are afraid of other countries using China as a battlefield, and we also hate anti-war conferences. We still seem to be "sleeping lions."

"Yellow Peril" can turn into "fortune," and awakened lions can also act. During the European War, we had workers who risked their lives for others, Qingdao was occupied, and we had children who could be carried upside down.

But to say that there is no place for us on the stage of the twentieth century is reasonable.

A Dissenting Opinion 242

— Zhi Li

Mr. Shi Zhecun laments the lack of vocabulary in the writings of today's youth and advises them to read "Zhuangzi" and "Wen Xuan." I beg to differ. I believe that the abundance or scarcity of vocabulary is actually due to the completeness or lack of common sense, and fundamentally, it is due to the amount of practical life experience. Simply reading a few books is in vain. The writing of "Zhuangzi" is produced by Zhuang Zhou's philosophical thought and actual knowledge. In his "Nourishing Life" section, the "Butcher Ding Dissects an Ox," the description of dissecting an ox can be said to be rich in vocabulary. May I ask Mr. Shi, where did these words come from? Could they come from someone who has never carefully observed someone dissecting an ox? For the average reader, it already takes a lot of effort to understand the words in Zhuangzi's articles today, and if there is no other basic knowledge, many chapters cannot be understood at all. Can they use the vocabulary in them at their disposal? As for "Wen Xuan," since it collects a large number of authors, the actual knowledge it contains is even broader, so the vocabulary is even richer, but those words are definitely not obtained by reading any books, most of them are created by the author based on actual knowledge. Just look at the San Du Liang Jing Fu, which has the richest vocabulary, and you will know.

The ancients did not have to rely on the books of their predecessors, and could create new words themselves. Today, knowledge is easy to acquire, and life is even more complex, but instead, we have to go to the books of our predecessors to find vocabulary. What do young people think of this opinion based on the theory of regression? Not necessarily very ancient people, even after the Tang and Song dynasties, there were still people who understood that the articles of Sima Qian had a strange spirit, which was helped by famous mountains and great rivers, but today people think that "Zhuangzi" and "Wen Xuan" are models for all ages.

Recently, the vocabulary in Chinese works is also really poor, far inferior to foreign works. But this reason lies in the lack of basic knowledge of Chinese people, while foreigners, because of the completeness of their education or the richness of their life, their works are so substantial. The greatness of Gorky's works is due to the "seeing a lot," and as for the Russian "Zhuangzi" and "Wen Xuan," they had little influence on him.

To describe factories, go to factories. To describe rural areas, go to rural areas. Those who understand botany should describe trees. Those who understand astronomy should describe the sky. Then the vocabulary will naturally be rich, the metaphors will naturally be appropriate, and the descriptions will naturally be wonderful. It is much better than having read "Zhuangzi" and "Wen Xuan." Many people notice the influence of old literature in Lu Xun's works, but why don't they see the influence of natural science and practical life experience in them?

Scholars like Mr. Shi Zhecun are indeed known for their rich vocabulary—vocabulary from ancient texts. But vocabulary is formal, and the content of our literary works is more important than form. Rather than appreciating carved, exquisite, but empty things, we would rather see works with substantial content and rough form. Like the shape of politics, today's literary rules are also gradually becoming stricter, and young people's creative activities in various aspects are intentionally or unintentionally being restricted by someone. The "mentor" system in the literary world will be restored. "Alas! I want to emulate the ancients' ability to create, but my fate does not meet the time. I want to follow what the people of today follow, but I am ashamed." (Gong Zizhen's Literary Style Admonition)

Letter to Mr. Li Liewen 243

— Shi Zhecun

— Also for Mr. Feng Zhiyu

Brother Liewen:

That day on the tram, I was in a hurry because I was going to the Minjiu Society bookstore to buy a book I liked, so I got off at Wangjiasha. But in the end, I didn't buy the book because the price didn't match, and I missed the opportunity to talk to you for a moment longer, which I regret very much.

Regarding the "Zhuangzi and Wen Xuan" issue, I have decided not to say anything more. Originally, when I filled out the form sent by the Dabao Evening News editorial department, it did not contain the seriousness that Mr. Feng's opinion showed. I am not saying that every young person must read these two books, nor am I saying that every young person only needs to read these two books, nor am I saying that I only have these two books to recommend. Probably the editor of the newspaper supplement wanted to add a little novelty to it, and the people filling it out mostly casually wrote down whatever books they thought might be worth reading. Had I known that writing this would cause such a big literary dispute, even if Mr. Cui Wanqiu, the editor of the Dabao Evening News supplement, had winked at me, I would not have written it. Today I saw a letter from Mr. Cao Juren to me in the fortieth issue of "Tao Sheng," the last sentence of which is: "Is there anything more beneficial to young people than these two books? Dare I ask." This question really made me laugh and cry. (Mr. Cao Juren's letter is very sincere, I will give him a reply, and maybe he will publish it in "Shou Sheng," I hope you take a look.)

I don't want to offend Mr. Zhizhiyu again, but I still have a few opinions regarding the three additional points he made in his "Old Issues" article!

(1) Mr. Feng said: "Some new youths can have old ideas, and some old forms can also contain new content." Yes, new youths can still have old ideas, so it seems that I, as a limb of the group of remnants, can also be left alone with old ideas. As for old forms also containing new content, it seems that it is okay to write ancient prose like "Zhuangzi," just look at its content.

(2) Mr. Feng said that he doesn't understand the difference between my advice to young people to read "Zhuangzi and Wen Xuan" and the examiners taking scholars based on their words. There is actually a clear distinction. The former is to offer one's own views to young people, and whether or not they accept it is up to the young people's freedom; the latter represents the entire class (Note: the class of officials.) and almost forces the entire youth to fill in the lyrics. (Unless this youth doesn't want to be an official).

(3) It is indeed ridiculous to say that Mr. Lu Xun's articles came from "Zhuangzi and Wen Xuan." I remember that I did not say such a thing. In my article, I cited Mr. Lu Xun as an example, intending to ask the anti-old youth to get a little literary cultivation from ancient books to help. Although Mr. Lu Xun has always advised young people to read more foreign books, this is because he believes that young people with new ideas can be trained from foreign books; as for thinking about young people from the perspective of writing articles (or literary cultivation) like me, Mr. Lu Xun has never opposed young people reading ancient books. Let me give two pieces of evidence: (1) "Reading less Chinese books will only result in not being able to write articles." (See page 4 of the Beixin edition of the Cover Collection,) This shows that Mr. Lu Xun also admitted that to be able to write articles, one should read more Chinese books. And this so-called Chinese book, judging from the above, does not seem to refer to vernacular documents. (2) "I am often asked, what books should I read to do literature?… I think if you want to do the old stuff, you might as well rely on Zhang Zhidong's 'Book List and Answers' to find your way." (See page 45 of the Beixin edition of Already Collected.)

Now, I think I should "stop" here. I once gave a letter to the editor of the Dabao Evening News supplement, and out of respect for Mr. Feng Zhiyu's good intentions, I asked permission to exchange two books to introduce to young people. Apart from writing a letter to Mr. Cao Juren, I have nothing to say about this "Zhuangzi and Wen Xuan" issue. I have seen text disputes on the wall of "Free Talk" several times, and I feel that each time they always become more and more emotional and further and further away from the topic, and even later some participants' motives are questionable. I don't want to be involuntarily drawn into the whirlpool, so I won't say anything more. Last night I used a ready-made gatha: This is also a right and wrong, That is also a right and wrong. Only without a view of right and wrong, Can one avoid right and wrong.

Is there anyone who can write seal characters? I would like to ask for a law to wave and stick it on the white wall. Shi Zhecun Shang (19th)

Communication from Ganpu (7) 244

— Aying

Brother ○○:

The salt manufacturing process was already discussed in the previous two letters. Now I want to continue by describing the general living conditions of the salt producing area of Ganpu and the salt workers.

The salt fields here are divided into three districts: East, West, and South. The East district is ten li long, the West district is two li long, and the South district is about one or two li long. The number of salt workers in the East district is seven or eight thousand, in the West district four or five thousand, and in the South district only a few hundred. The number of salt kilns is eighteen in the East district, ten in the West district, and three in the South district. According to my investigation, the annual salt production is about 13,000 yin, equivalent to 19,000 dan, with an official price of 2.4 yuan per dan, valued at 456,000 silver dollars. Each district has a kiln director (灶董), one for the East district, and one shared between the Southwest districts. The selection of these kiln directors is similar to electing representatives during the National Assembly; they are chosen through joint consultation between the government and salt merchants. These individuals usually have three qualifications: first, they have had prior dealings with government officials and salt merchants; second, their family finances are reasonably sound; and third, they are more knowledgeable than the average salt worker. What these kiln directors are like? I won't say, you probably already know. In name, they are representatives of the salt workers, but in reality, they do not represent them. Instead, they simply follow the orders of government officials and salt merchants, helping them to impose levies and taxes. It is said that one of them is relatively good and can represent the salt workers to some extent, but I don't know to what degree. Such figures are the leaders of all the salt workers. Therefore, the salt workers here are often starving and have no food to eat, while taxes are still increased, and the kiln directors do nothing about it.

In Ganpu, the salt workers do not entirely rely on salt production for a living. They also do other things to supplement their income. For example, people in the Southeast districts also farm. At the same time, in addition to salt production and farming, salt workers in the East district also cultivate land, plant trees, and about three hundred people also engage in fishing. In the West district, only a few salt workers own mountains and fields, and some near the North-South Lake also fish. In addition, salt workers naturally have many side businesses and by-products, such as silkworm rearing, etc., but the main ones are firewood and hemp. However, there is a peculiar phenomenon in Ganpu that must be mentioned, which is that regardless of whether they are salt workers or farmers, they do not grow vegetables in the summer and autumn. You can't buy vegetables; if you really want to eat them, you have to gather wild herbs yourself. This is because their fields are used for other purposes at this time. They only grow vegetables as usual in winter. The salt workers actually suffer a lot, although in any district, we don't see any thatched huts, but all tiled houses. The largest number of salt workers are shoulder-pole peddlers. They sometimes help others with work, sometimes sell lightly taxed salt, and often go hungry. Salt workers do not all own salt kilns or kiln shares. Generally, the brine they collect is either sold to the "Chaofeng," i.e., the so-called "kiln directors," or they rent the kiln directors' kilns to burn themselves. However, this is ultimately a small number. Most sell the brine. Some salt workers have actually borrowed money from the Chaofeng at high interest before the brine is collected, and repay it with a lot of brine. The Chaofeng own many salt ponds, storing the brine inside. When the salt in the warehouses is sold out, they use oil barrels to pump it out and burn it. Usually, they seal it with mud tendons. If you come to Ganpu, you can see that the kiln areas are full of brine barrels everywhere. Some are beside the road, and some are in the middle of the road. What you are walking on is a road, but below the road are brine barrels. It can truly be said that salt is everywhere. Moreover, next to this, you may sometimes see rectangular, lidless boxes with wooden edges of about one or two inches, filled with salt brine, placed under the sunlight. This is called "sun-dried salt." Salt is sometimes produced by "drying" instead of "burning."

The overall aspects of the salt workers' lives are roughly like this. The rest, we'll talk about next time.

Two Brothers (3) 245

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

Jean had been, from a young age, a model of gentleness, goodness and character; while Pierre, constantly hearing others praise this older child, gradually became agitated. In his view, Jean's gentleness was weakness, goodness was stupidity, and good intentions were blindness. His parents were peaceful people, only hoping that their two children could obtain a respectable but ordinary position, scolding him for being fickle, ... for getting excited, scolding him for those failed attempts, and all the ambitious, yet unattainable aspirations.

When he grew up, people no longer said to him, "Look at Jean, learn from him!" But every time he heard others repeatedly saying, "Jean did this, did that," he understood the meaning of these words and the implied hints they contained. Their mother was an upper-class woman, a frugal, and emotionally sensitive bourgeois, with a naturally gentle and meticulous character. She constantly mediated the small animosities that arose between the two sons every day from the most minor matters of their shared life. And at this time, there was also a minor event that made her uneasy, she feared that things would become troublesome, because last winter, when her two children were finishing their specialized studies, she met a neighbor, Mrs. Luziemi, the widow of a deep-sea ship captain who had died at sea two years ago. This young widow was very young, only twenty-three years old, an intelligent woman who instinctively understood life, like a free beast, as if she had seen, experienced, understood and measured all events, she could criticize with a sound, narrow, but well-intentioned intelligence. She was accustomed to running over to the homes of these two kind neighbors every evening to have a cup of tea and chat for a while.

Mr. Roland, whose obsession with being a sailor was constantly stirring up, often inquired about the deceased captain in front of his new female friend, and she would talk about her husband, her husband's travels, and those old stories, etc. She spoke so eloquently, fully expressing the character of a woman who loved life, respected the dead, was rational and could be patient.

After the two sons returned, finding that this beautiful widow often came to their home, they immediately began to flirt with this woman, the main motive not being to make the woman like them, but to defeat their brother.

Their mother, who was prudent and practical, desperately hoped that one of the two could conquer this widow, because this young woman was very rich. But she also hoped that the other would not be in any grief.

Talks

Creation, Imitation, Enjoyment 270

- Guang Han

Everyone knows that mankind is a product of culture. It is because of culture that we humans are "different from animals," and so we have not sought the consent of plants, animals, and minerals, and have self-respected as "the holiest of all things." However, we humans, on the one hand, have the right to enjoy culture, and on the other hand, are also obligated to create it. Because to enjoy, we need to create; with creation, we can then enjoy. But let's take a look: how many people in the world today can exercise the right to enjoy and also fulfill the duty to create?

You don't have to be a Western worshiper. Can you deny that many modern cultural elements were invented by Westerners? Whether in material or spiritual aspects, just to give a few examples: the former like electric lights, trains, ships, and various machines; the latter like various new ideas and new academic disciplines. Which of these is not a contribution of the Westerners? Speaking impartially, we are enjoying this beautiful culture today, directly and indirectly, all thanks to their gifts. Their achievements in modern culture can truly be considered great; although their efforts, in some cases, may inevitably be flawed, but that is another question.

Speaking of Japan, they certainly do not have as much creativity as Westerners; but their imitation skills are truly astonishing. When someone invents something new, they cannot invent it themselves, but they can imitate it. Not only do they imitate it until it is exactly the same as yours, but they also manufacture it more exquisitely and skillfully than yours. Sometimes they can even discover a new thing through imitation, which is truly remarkable. This is solely in terms of material culture; as for spiritual culture, they have made not a few contributions to modern new ideas and new academic disciplines.

As for China, we cannot create, nor can we imitate; we can only sit back and enjoy the fruits of others' labor. We are smart enough; we are unwilling to bother to waste time and effort inventing. Nor do we deign to be so unprogressive as to imitate others' ready-made products. We have plenty of money. Today someone invents a motorcycle, and we immediately have a car to ride tomorrow. Tomorrow someone invents architecture, and we immediately have a Western-style house to live in the day after tomorrow. New academic disciplines and new ideas are introduced, and our grand works are published accordingly; our beliefs also begin to waver. In short, everything in modern civilization that others can enjoy, we can also enjoy in the same way. What else is lacking? Aren't we satisfied yet? Do we still want to disturb our minds, trouble our hands and feet, and personally learn to create and imitate?

Enough! What is learned here are three different national characteristics. Westerners are rich in creativity, so their culture can leap forward thousands of miles, becoming more and more new every day, and progressing endlessly. The Japanese are rich in imitation ability, so they can also keep pace with Europe and America, full of vitality. Only we Chinese know how to enjoy, so everything is lagging behind, and we are running down the road to death and destruction. From this, we can understand that a national characteristic has a very significant relationship with the culture of a nation-state, and we must not ignore it. I am not just speaking fine words that please everyone, or digging into our own shortcomings; because the facts are clear evidence and there is no need to conceal them. I hope that the people of the country will wake up as soon as possible, and quickly improve our national characteristics from the root!

The Poor and Love 271

- Qian Xu

Recently, I watched "The River All Red." It seems to me that whether poor people can actually fall in love has definitely become a problem.

"The River All Red" tells us that "if a poor person talks about love, he is simply looking for his own death." However, the love of the poor in "The River All Red" is successful, because although the sudden fire at the end burns the poor and the woman to ashes together, the fire comes so "suddenly" that we regard it as "far-fetched," a "tail" that is forcibly attached. If we cut off this far-fetched tail happily, then it will show the standard of successful love for the poor.

However, can the poor actually talk about love? Let's not talk about how serious the current social situation is, how bankrupt the rural economy is, or how many unemployed people there are in the cities; even if a singer is willing to condescend and look favorably upon a poor boy and talk about love, on the poor person's

Page 22

side, he is concerned about whether there is enough bread, so where does he get so much leisure? Therefore, this argument, which deviates from the facts, only shows its "incomprehensibility."

However, whether people are poor or rich, male or female, when they reach a certain age, they naturally have an urgent desire in their hearts—that is to say, when they develop to a certain state physiologically, they will feel a kind of inexplicable "sexual" hunger. Therefore, "boredom" occurs. Thus, in order to dispel this "boredom," solve this "hunger," and satisfy the physiological "urgent desire," and on the one hand, to cater to the trend of the times, they "naturally" take the path of "love."

The poor person's current difficulty is "poverty," and the "path of love" is built on beautiful faces and sparkling money. The obvious contradiction leaves the poor with no room to intervene and is destined to fail before they realize their mistake. Therefore, poor people can only move forward and temporarily forget about "love," even though they have reached the age where they need love.

Moreover, the result of love can only hinder the motivation to move forward and increase the economic burden. It is absolutely unsuitable for poor people, and even more unsuitable for poor people who are struggling to move forward. Although there are also some advocates of love above all else who say: "Love can help people to have an interest in being human, can urge the progress of their careers, and can be regarded as a kind of motivation." Indeed, but it must have the condition of "not being poor" and must have "assets" as a backup; otherwise, it is still utopia and dreaming.

What's more, "love" is fundamentally a leisure game for those who are "propertied" and "have leisure," a tool to exert their "property" and "leisure" authority. If a poor person wants to squeeze onto this stage, it is simply very likely to fall down, and at the same time, he is in danger of falling to his death.

Therefore, my conclusion is: poor people can only attack their careers and solve the problem of "poverty." If you really want to step onto the stage of "love," it is not too late to wait until you are "not poor."

Because "poor people" and "love" are fundamentally unrelated.

A Salty Farce 272

- Shen Min

A friend who owns a signboard shop asked me to write a large character for a signboard a few days ago. This signboard was custom-made by a certain pickled meat shop. Carelessly, I accidentally wrote the word "salted" instead of "pickled." After writing it, I was in a hurry and did not check it, so I gave it to him. The friend in the signboard shop was illiterate, so he did not notice it. He followed the example and made the signboard, and then sent it to the pickled meat shop, hanging it high above the door, waiting for the shop's opening. The owner of the shop, a Ningbo native, looked up and burst into flames. "You, his mother, bitch born, what are you doing? Who wrote this salty meat shop signboard?" He grabbed the owner of the signboard shop, and the two twisted each other all the way to my residence, launching a punitive expedition. At this time, I already knew that it was because of the mistake of a single "salted" word. But I was not willing to show weakness, so I could only make the best of a bad situation and adapt to circumstances. He said that I opened a pickled meat shop, why did you write salty meat shop? Aren't you touching my bad luck? I said to him, "Don't just get angry, things must be practical, there are words to say, and reasons to argue. Isn't pickled meat and salted meat one and the same? Moreover, the restaurant serves salty meat and tofu soup, dry salty meat, and I have never heard of pickled meat and tofu soup, or dry pickled meat." He said, "That's not how it's said. Everyone knows that the salty meat shop is opened in the human flesh market near the Niutou Company on Baxian Bridge! Aren't you intentionally making fun of me and teasing me?" I said, "This is a common saying among idlers. In which meat market have you ever seen a salty meat shop signboard? This reason has no basis. Moreover, your shop sells salted fish, salted eggs, salted vegetables, salted jellyfish, etc., and you definitely can't change them to pickled fish, pickled eggs, pickled vegetables, etc." At this time, he was rendered speechless by my refutation. He was stunned. Later, he said that after this signboard was hung, it caused a sensation far and wide, and people came to visit in an endless stream, which made me very embarrassed. This is a matter of reputation! I said, "Don't get me wrong. This phenomenon is excellent. This is obviously because the signboard I wrote is special, and it is also a very wonderful publicity effect. Generally, when a new shop opens, it can cause a sensation far and wide, and people come to visit in an endless stream, which is a sign of prosperous business and abundant wealth!" When he heard these two auspicious words, he smiled and left. A salty storm had just subsided. Sure enough, there was an unexpected effect. The day before yesterday, I happened to pass by the shop. I saw people chopping salted meat, so crowded that they could not stand. Whether it was for the publicity of a salty word is also impossible to investigate.

Shanghai people call the third-class meat market a salty meat shop. I don't know what the meaning is. It's really inexplicable.

Zhabei Eulogy 273

- Wen Bing

The vast and prosperous Shanghai seems to refer entirely to the concessions. Shanghai is so worthy of praise! The concessions are even more worthy of eulogy! Writers, how many are racking their brains to write "Sketches of Nanjing Road," "Nights on Avenue Joffre!" Beautiful, happy, all the colorful scenes are poured out only in the concessions!

Zhabei, because it is still a piece of Chinese land, is so dirty, so desolate! Oh, this is simply the desert outside the Arctic Circle, the sand base in the oasis. Disappointing, dazzling, how can it be worthy of a latrine in the concessions?

And ask, who doesn't have such a feeling? Who doesn't harbor such contempt? Oh, is Zhabei really like this? No, absolutely not! If we were not full of some kind of poison, if we had not put on colored glasses, and also possessed the marrow of Chinese national character, we should be able to thoroughly understand that this is precisely where we deserve to praise!

Although the streets here are very dirty, and the market here is very desolate, this is just like a person dragging old clothes. Even his body and his soul are noble, pure, vigorous, and moving forward courageously!

Here there is no shadowy figure of high-class Chinese who flatter foreigners and seek glory, nor the rampant acts of very poisonous capitalists, nor the sinister laughter of unscrupulous merchants, nor the activities of modern gentlemen in the sex industry, nor the intoxicating murmurings of refined gentlemen. What exists is the activities of the common people, the struggles of the coolies. They are working to continue their own lives, for the reunion of their families, for the duties of mankind, for the future of the nation-state. Who has shed the disguise of the hypocritical identity of that word, is using their hands, using their feet, vigorously moving forward,
