Various Kinds of Fraud 275

— Years Bing-Ding

Besides earning money through legitimate professions, there are truly many ways to obtain money in Shanghai. Swindling, stealing, cheating, begging, all sorts of tricks and endless variations. If one were to compile a special book on this, wouldn't it run into millions of words? However, although there are many kinds and various methods, their consistent purpose is to get other people's money without exchanging their own "labor" or "capital." Perhaps this is a phenomenon of "civilized evolution"!

(1)

When we are sitting in a tram or rickshaw, perhaps your hat will disappear into thin air, and the money in your pocket will vanish without a trace. Especially when you, sir, arrive at the Shiliupu Wharf on a Ningbo steamer at dawn, you may encounter some "chop-splitting" fellows who either grab your rickshaw, demanding a few cents for road money; or block your way, robbing your luggage. This is the first bit of money that a "Ningbo newcomer" should pay upon arriving in Shanghai, and it should be paid without delay. It's truly an unspeakable predicament.

(2)

"Friend! Help a little!" "Know what's good for you, or you'll eat a raw bullet! Quickly hand over the money!" Night-walking friends living in Shanghai can often encounter the above phrases. How would you handle it, sir? This is to test your mettle. Generally, ninety-nine percent of the time, you, sir, will suffer a loss. If you're lucky, you can offer them a yuan or two as tribute. Or, they might invite you, sir, to "peel a pig," leaving you stark naked to return to your esteemed wife, who might even think you escaped after being subjected to forced sodomy. (Stealing your clothes is called "peeling a pig"; snatching your hat is called "grabbing a crow"; pulling your rickshaw across a bridge is called "pulling a yellow ox." Their humor surpasses that of Boerne, even better than Lin Yutang.)

(3)

We Ningbo people have a highly successful fellow-countryman association in Shanghai. Who doesn't know about it? Who hasn't heard of it? Who would have known there was also a tiny fellow-countryman association, so admirable that it makes people want to prostrate themselves in reverence! It turns out that this small fellow-countryman association has a very perfect organization and very simple articles of association. Although there are fewer than a hundred members, each one is a descendant of scholars and the sons of wealthy men. Because "wealthy people take turns every ten years, and fortune and poverty rotate in the world," inevitably these young masters, feeling adrift in Shanghai, only desire a life of seclusion and leisure and are unwilling to peddle their wares in the marketplace. Therefore, they founded this "Lumpen Proletariat Fellow-Countryman Association" to pursue a life of "seclusion" and "retirement." It is said that the association's address is in a small inn on XX Road. Every morning, the chairman convenes a temporary executive meeting to discuss the association's affairs for the day. After the discussion, Member XXX is appointed as "ferry and transport guest"; Member XXX is appointed as "rear road street runner"; Member XXX, the stock exchange. Once the appointment order is issued, they each set off without delay. It turns out that these places are easy to find old friends or relatives of their fathers' generation, or those with family connections, or old acquaintances, and naturally, it's easy to borrow money from them. After the day's work is completed, they all hand over the money they have obtained to the chairman. Apart from the day's expenses, it is divided fairly and evenly, and each member then happily goes off to do their "playing the transverse flute" work. The next day, they still work hard at their divinely ordained routine, heading off to work separately. Therefore, this "Lumpen Proletariat Fellow-Countryman Association" is flourishing! Song Lian said: "Heaven and earth are the coffin, the sun and moon are the jade for the mouth"; the members of this fellow-countryman association truly have this kind of demeanor!

Imperialism After a Round of Violence 276

— Zeqing

One Sunday evening, I went to the Da Jiangnan Restaurant to see a friend, but the appointed time had not yet arrived. So I wandered around Beijing Road, idly gazing at the red and green traffic lights, the towering, wooden-faced Indian police officers, the powdered-face, rouged-lip courtesans, the wandering, frivolous young masters, the beast-like capitalist's automobiles, the sharp, haggard faces of beggars under unkempt hair, and so on. Ah! What a rugged and sinful urban night!

"Sir, how do I get to Tilanqiao from here?"

A low voice brushed past my hearing.

At the same time, someone seemed to be tugging at my sleeve. When I turned my head, what came into view was a thirteen- or fourteen-year-old boy with a simple and honest appearance, wearing a student uniform of rice-white "liberty cloth." He was carrying a newspaper satchel (?) under his arm. One could tell at a glance that he was a faithful elementary school student. (?)

"Tilanqiao? It's far! You go to the front, steal a chicken, and take the No. 7 tram. Keep going straight...".

"No! Sir. I'm not taking the tram. I want to walk there. Please, is this the road to get there?"

"Walk there? It's very far! How can I explain it clearly? You don't know the way. It's so late, how can you walk there? Why do you want to walk to Tilanqiao?"

"My home is in Tilanqiao. School let out today. My sister and I went to Sincere Company to buy things. But after getting off the tram, there was a crowd. I couldn't find my sister. I don't know the way either, and the money is with my sister, so I want to run back!"

"Oh! How can I do that? You're so young. How can you run such a long distance? Since that's the case, I'll give you these coins to take the tram back!"

"How can I do that? Thank you too much..." He bashfully lowered his head with childlike innocence.

"Don't be polite. Take it! It's nothing!" I then gave him twenty or so copper coins from my purse and directed him to hurry and take the No. 7 tram heading north.

When I came out of the Da Jiangnan, the clock already pointed to eleven o'clock. However, the people in this big city who were used to nightlife were still as noisy, clamorous, hurried, and bustling as during the day... Dragging my tired body, I turned right towards Nanjing Road—the goal was to get some refreshments.

"Sir! How do I get to Tilanqiao from here?"

This sound brushed past my hearing, and I found it really strange. Why are so many people asking about Tilanqiao today? When I turned my face, I was almost startled into shouting. Wasn't this the child I gave money to on Beijing Road? When he saw my face, he was also particularly flustered. He ran away into the crowd like a wisp of smoke.

"Ah! City! Sinful city! This poor, already dead human heart! Who ultimately defiled his pure, innocent soul?" On the way back, I pondered this over and over.

Struggle 277

— Suxin

The meaning of the two words "struggle" seems to imply that humans or any animal, suffering the pain of being bound, makes a final effort to achieve freedom or survival. Look at chickens or ducks among poultry; when they are about to be slaughtered, their feet are tied with rope; they will definitely struggle and scream there, hoping to obtain a final chance at survival or freedom. Seeing this expression is indeed somewhat pitiful, but in the end, they still cannot escape people's knives because their ability to struggle cannot resist the power of people wanting to kill them, so they can only be slaughtered by humans.

Looking at a country, isn't it always like this? Look at our China. In the past hundred years or so, we have repeatedly failed in diplomacy; therefore, we have lost land, opened treaty ports, established concessions, and signed all kinds of unequal treaties. Even last year, we lost the Northeast. The crisis is imminent, like a rich man encountering bandits and robbers who want both his property and his life, and will not stop until the rich man dies and his wealth is exhausted. Then, if we don't struggle out of the hands of the bandits, can the rich man—China's life and property—be preserved intact?

China is said to be one of the nominally republican and independent countries in the world, not subject to the control of any country. However, looking at the above situation, China is simply surrounded by bandit-like and robber-like powers. How dangerous is the property of the Chinese people? How unfree are all our actions? Therefore, as long as these surrounding bandits—the powers—are not removed one day, China will not have a free and comfortable life for a single day.

Hey! Those young masters embracing women and those gentlemen dancing modern dances with dance girls, and those comrades whose gun muzzles are pointed inward; wake up! Everyone rise up and perk up your spirits, struggle for our own country; break free from the intangible and tangible shackles of those robber-like powers; seize back our property, preserve our lives; and achieve our true, complete freedom and a strong and prosperous country. Wake up! Everyone strive to make a final struggle!

Drama

Juvenile Thief 279

— Yucheng

Yan Shu's courtroom has an unspeakable atmosphere of gloom. The bailiff brings up an underage child. He looks only fourteen or fifteen years old. He stands in the dock with a calm demeanor, showing no signs of fear. (Judge) (After asking his name and age, shakes his head repeatedly and says:) Why don't you learn the right path at such a young age and instead do this illegal thing! You must know: snatching hats may be a small matter, but the crime is the same as other thefts.

(Child) To be honest, Your Honor, I have committed this crime several times already. Knowing it is illegal, I have no choice but to do it!

(Judge) You wretch, you dare to rant here! You won't learn to be good, so I sentence you to six months!

(Judge) (Enraged) What nonsense are you talking about? That's outrageous! Do you think the sentence is too light? Hmph, I'll add another six months! You are so bold at such a young age, won't you kidnap and kill people when you grow up?

(Child) (With boundless emotion:) Your Honor, don't blame me for committing crimes as a child, you can only blame our country for being so disappointing! Think about it, it's impossible to resist being hungry and cold; moreover, I have an elderly grandmother and a disabled father. Do you expect the whole family to go without food and clothing? Alas!...

(Judge) Couldn't you do some other business?

(Child) Bystanders may say it's easy, but when you are in that situation, there is simply no way! Haven't I graduated from elementary school? Don't I know some basic common sense? But there is no place for me in society. I lack the capital to start a business. With no money and no power, what else can I do but steal?

(Judge) (Lost for words) I won't talk nonsense with you any longer; (waving his hand at the bailiff,) take him away!
